Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie;	And in this way tell the patient to apply a fresh and dry leaf of lime tree, and grind it well with a little grease, and put on the back and thighs and legs where the pain is, and tie it.
et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	and he leaves it for three hours, by which time the pain has subsided.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then make him enter a warm bath until the heart is slightly warmed, and then make him enter a bed, and the pain will disappear entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And advise that no one should use such cauteries or medicines unless after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout;	And Dioscorides says that when the vein is cauterized with the heat of a goat's horn, it helps greatly.
et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	and it must be done in this way with the cauteries.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another and beat the old oil, and put it on the fossa that is between the thumb and the other one called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains;	After taking dry goat's horn, and putting it in the fire until it becomes charcoal, and then placing it on a cloth, and leaving it until it is cool.
et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee;	and repeat this process, and do not stop until you think it is near the ribs, and that the pain has ceased.
et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	And this method of cauterization is called "goat's-foot cauterization".
de la dolor dou dos	of the great pain of two
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether from falling or from impact or from too great evacuation, or from similar matter spread coldly, none of these situations is worth cauterizing, because it is better for those who have recently been infused with cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir;	It is necessary to apply foul-smelling pills or similar things on the affected area, three lines wide, where the pain is located, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to its virtue and quantity that the wound can bear.
et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»;	And it should be made with cauterizations according to the cauterization called "spiked".
et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make three or four cauterizations according to the cauterization called "claw-like" in this form.
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor;	Often this disease comes to small children, and the signs of onset are that they have stiffness in their neck when moving, and fear.
et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	and you tread on the last spinous process of the back and in us the appearance that comes above the other spinous processes.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see it and you see it healed, if you cauterize it with this fire cautery in this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery grasps every part of the spinous process.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, if you cauterize around the spinous process with this fire cautery holding II lines or III, and they are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After healing the limb as we have said, according to how it is healthy, and be careful not to apply the cauterization in a place that is swollen with nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere:	When joint pain from moisture that is spread to each limb of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which they properly call «podagra», and when it is a cold cause and cures of medicines cannot cure it, then it is treated by cauterization in this way:
fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	make the most of cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and the cauterizing iron should be in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a reason to hold the face down with the sharp instrument, then apply the entire cauterization process that is called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire;	And if the pains come from the knees and other joints, and they often do, then apply the fire cautery over each joint three or four times on each part, with olive oil throughout.
et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you have more skill, then do more, but do not hold your hand too far unless the pain is already well-managed.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the jaw and back, then administer the cauterization that we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes;	And if the pains are in the hands, then apply it around the knuckle two lines deep;
et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main;	and if there is still no pain, then apply it over each joint and on the hair of the hand;
et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	and if the pains come from the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and apply good management to the pain and appropriate medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you provide good care and purge the humor, it will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor;	When a fracture occurs in anger, and the bowels descend to the groin, and this is newly, so it is necessary that when you see it to heal, that it does not move that day;
et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre;	and that he uses things that lower the abdomen, so that the bowels do not descend from his abdomen;
aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors;	after the fracture is seated on his back between your hands, and he commands that he tinges his shoulder until the bowels are repaired, and he pulls it to his sides, and signs of this are similar to half a circle above the chest;
puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then heat the cauterizing iron of this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	so long as it is white and sheds senselessness.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu;	Then reset the dislocated joint;
et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier;	and the assistant wipes his hand over it so they do not return.
et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains;	And work well on the thighs with the hairs, and put disinfectant on him on the muscle and on the skin above the thighs, and the other on the lowest part that cleans his hands.
puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os;	Then place the cauterizing iron on the sign at all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, then continue another until you come just to the bone.
et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere;	and you must guard carefully that the pus does not escape while you are performing the cauterization.
que tu ne le brulasses;	that you do not burn it.
et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	and that by this means the hairs do not die, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And if you do not come to the bone with the fire cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure;	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be delicate according to their size, and for large people also large according to their size;
aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	after three days, care for the wound of the cautery with butter until the scar is formed.
aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee;	after the care of other remedies until it is healed, and grind the hairs 40 days on their back until the wound is well healed.
et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	and it is necessary that its [the patient's] restraints be loosened long enough, so that the bile does not spill when he attempts to go into the chambers.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors;	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, let him be given a well-made bandage, and for another forty days.
et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire;	and let him have good rest, that he works little and avoids too much overeating and drinking, and too much loud noise.
et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And when he does this teaching, if he is entirely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after the treatment of cutting into his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the tearing of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When wounds come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, let him have the fire cauterization according to its quantity, and let it be applied to the third part of the wound.
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	After the treatment according to what we have said;
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the fire cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is to bend and make a line across the width of the rip, and another one after, and keep your hand on all the cauterizing iron.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and quieter.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, whether to fall or to pierce, and this pain lasts long, and the medical cure is not effective, then it must be cauterized with the cauterizing iron called "poins", and the cauteries should follow the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and strength and location of twists and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	if it is healthy after the first cauterization, it is good;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	if not, begin another cauterization above the first one, for it is usually the case that it should be done to the member that is nearest, because it is necessary to do the cauterizations until the hairs are healed.
de meselerie	of mutilation
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Mutilations are never treated with cauterization by great help, and even the disease that comes from the putrefaction of pus and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	If you see that it is not being cauterized, take care if the disease is at the beginning, and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will not spread throughout the wound, then make five cauterizations above the head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I place the head to the north, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the temples.
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	and II above the two horns, and I behind the hitterel.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	and let your hand be so that the cautery comes close to the bone, and as much as the scabs come out so that the vapors of the large humors can escape.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	and cauterize over the small one according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the injury is scattered everywhere;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it is clearly present, then you must cauterize with these cautery that we have said or chief, and the cautery in the nose, and II cauterizes above the spine of the neck, and VI cauterizes above the spine of the back, and I large above the buttocks and I other below, and II above the two shoulders;
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	and II above the ears, and II above the tendons of the worst kind, and I above each joint of the hands and feet, and above the wounds of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	and guard against the nerves that are above the lower back, so you do not burn them.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	and never make a fire cauterization above the bone of the thumb, and one on the other bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And it is said that the more you make a fire cauterization, the less you help, and move it away from the patient.
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And it is said that the hairs do not feel pain as much as healthy people do, because the body is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	It is necessary that the cauterization be large and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in the ways of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the wound with flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then you should cauterize the member according to its size and smallness.
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	and either the cauterization goes deep into the flesh of the member;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of wounds until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And never cauterize by hand and at the wrist and back, at the end of the member that makes the member immobile, and thus if it is ossified the inflammation;
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and no one should interfere with it unless they know the members and the veins moving through the body.
de albaras	do not comment on whether the translation is accurate or
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease known as «albaras» is awakened, and medical treatment does not help, then cauterize with a cautery a little in front, according to the amount of the skin that is affected, until the whiteness is removed, and it is moved its color;
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	then the cure of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of pigeon and blood of almond, of each one a part;
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be mixed together, and let it be bound with a cloth, and let it be applied to the limb until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears at the beginning, and you see it stop spreading, then cauterize it with a cauterizing iron that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And all the wise people said that one should also do a fire cauterization at the center of the chancre.
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And this does not seem good to me, because I think it will not be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never seen it happen.
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And the more important thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cauterizing iron called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it takes a long time to die or because of the excess that it causes or because of the age of the malady when they are old (that is, too old) and they have little blood, or for lack of tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you see it happening quickly:
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	then cauterize around the wound with many small cauteries by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	after leaving it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierce through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization from where this is the form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cauteries have perforated the skin, and be such that the cauteries feel it beforehand in a similar manner as the course of the pus is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment until they are completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire by iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another way of disease is called "corrodens", and is nothing but a moisture in the member, as it corrupts the members like dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this disease in the limb that can suffer cauteries and fire together, then heat the small and sharp cauteries greatly according to what is needed for the limb or the disease.
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	after cauterizing all parts until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, that everything that is corrupted be removed completely.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it three days, and apply the cauterized lead above the wounds, suffering great pain with oil until all the charred flesh is removed and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of wounds, they generate pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if you see after three days that healthy pus does not rise, it is good.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if it does not, then restart the cauterization above the part that is remaining decayed.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this wound has never been treated with medicine in place of fire cauterization;
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	But all fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already mentioned the treatment of medicine in the division:
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take it when you have the opportunity.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of the joints which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that at the feet by deficiency, a disease arises which is called "clubfoot" according to our understanding, and it is a great disfigurement which makes the foot look ugly.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauteries of this disease are in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and ice-hot cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cauterization is such that you heat it as if it were a pen of lead, and it should be made of good iron at the measure that it can penetrate the nail from all parts, and that it has narrow margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After you put everything on top of the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the end of the nail.
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and let it stay there for three days until it begins to rot.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a poultice of wild, crushed herbs with yarn, and leave the poultice on all night, and the nail will fall off and be pulled out from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the limb of inflammation by applying warmth until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they are converted by the wound, and often in the hands and feet, then it is necessary that you reapply cauterization with very hot fire.
et est en teil maniere:	and is in a similar manner:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	Take a needle of iron or steel, or a pen of quill, and place it over the nail and the wart, that is to say, prick the warts.
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And place the needle over it so that it pierces all around, then put a drop of hot wax, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the needle comes to the root of the nail, and find the hot wax penetrating deeply just at the root;
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	and bear the pain a little from the burning of the hot wax for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	then let it remain thus, and it will fall off at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Then do another one, until you have checked all those that are in the body, then cure the wounds that cause harm to the heart.
li cure dou trembler	cure the patient of trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When some tremble from cold or fever and chills or other, it is necessary that you make four burns or four above the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine.
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one or two below the belly, and one above the stomach at the olive cauterization;
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	it will let the tremble, and hasten the health from the disease of cold.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	No times have appeared from before with the body covered in wounds or pustules that come from large rotten substances.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	if it is necessary at the first when they appear that one make cauterization above each head of the pustule:
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	a thin cauterization of birch, of which the point should be held in the fire, or of the root of aristolochia long, or at the lens cauterization.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never use cauterization at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and it cannot grow more, but is destroyed by the excess from which they come, and are healed.
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	But it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surrounding parts, or to the incision of the abscess, or to the cauterization of the member, and similar things.
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	And it is a very painful thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And whenever it happens to anyone, you must quickly place your finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very tightly until the bleeding stops from your finger, and no more comes out.
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then apply the fire cautery with various sizes of blistering olive oil beads, both small and large, until they are all red.
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then apply I, whether large or small depending on the wound and where the artery is located, and place the fire cautery above that vein where you hold your hand, and keep the fire cautery as long as the wound does not bleed too much.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the first one fails and you lift your other hand above the vein, and the cauterizer is extinguished, then quickly take the other cauterizers that are at the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the wound is completely healed.
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	And be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes from the wound.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	and it is said that when without cutting the artery, one cannot smell it immediately when the artery is large, unless by one of the four methods that we have mentioned.
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	or by fire cauterization, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strong force of thread, or by medicines placed above that have the power to smell blood.
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	and it should be tied and held firmly in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers the tightening of ropes or other things overheated, or similar things, does not benefit unless not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if it has happened to anyone and they have no remedy present, then they should place their finger index above the wound of the vein as we have mentioned, and well strain until it is smelled over the wound and over the vein;
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	and it should not be moved, but it should be massaged with cold frequently until it is very cold and the wound is frozen and filled and closed.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	and make inquiries about the cause of which he should use cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of remedies for tails
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cauteries or burning medicines, and the questions and causes and instruments and forms of cauteries;
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	and I have placed that chapter on the shoulder joints down to the feet, and I will go to this chapter by the same way because it is easier to find out what we want.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore as I begin this chapter, it is necessary, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things;
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many ways of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	if they come from such people who have become so with their disease that they die immediately due to the fear of their disease, and the greatness of its evil.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	and one must fear these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these there are those who give you understanding, and say:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am a gardener.
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the disease is difficult to treat.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	It should only be granted to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your convenience, and do not open wildly but wisely of what you are certain and have taken and lost.
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your diseases that health may be converted.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And this will help you to gain good reputation, and glory, and memory for the long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lords grant you good understanding and straightness, and if you wish to breathe from the holy inspiration of His hand, indeed.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have ordered you to read this chapter by examining other chapters, according to what is before or after the chapter on cauteries, which I have previously provided from head to foot, so that you can find it more easily.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head is full of sharp points.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	Know that this disease often comes to infants at birth, and when the neck is held too tightly in the child;
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	And never is there a reason given that one might not be able to.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	And I have never seen this disease except in children, and all those that I have seen died from it.
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	Therefore, it seems to me that it is better to avoid this work in such treatments.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw a child who was suffering from this disease, and the head became increasingly swollen each day until it could no longer support itself.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	And it was believed that the moisture caused its death, and this moisture is gathered outside of the bone above the sinus, between the gum and the bone.
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and the work is such that if moisture is between the bone and the joint, and abscesses are small, you should make an incision in the head of the bone wide;
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and it should be as long as ours, until the moisture flows out;
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	and then in the shape of a space:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more extensive, and the abscess is larger, then make two cuts in the shape of a cross, according to this form.
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	and if the moisture is outside the bone, and the signs that you see the commissures of the head open from each part, and the sharp pain when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not return to you:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	if it is necessary that you make three incisions in the head of the bone in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	After applying bandages and powders to the wounds, and putting wine and oil on them, leave them like this until the fifth hour.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then remove the bandages, and cure the wound with tents and poultices, and leave the shoulder equally strained, and feed the patient dried meat to relieve the moisture until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another way of incision is that you look at the size of the abscess and the sharpness of the needle;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never the same.
aucune fois derrier;	never behind.
aucune fois en destre;	no time on the right;
et aucune fois en senestre.	and no time on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Then cut open where the abscess is open, and fill the sore, and make it according to what you have the power to do;
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	and be careful not to cover the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	and bring out blood, so that the hairs do not die from the separation of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of return
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When it happens to anyone with a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or in the pupil, and the disease is ancient, and medical treatment does not help much, then the cure is to cauterize with what they cover the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	Therefore, although you cover it, the hairs must do their own thing;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	then rub the sore with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then hold the hairs to all the cloth;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look at the vein that is bleeding, and the vessels on both sides are behind the ears, and they are not yet stopped.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then sign the vessels of the artery, then cut both with a sharp knife until the wound reaches the bone, and it should be through the wide part of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, push the adhesive away from the artery and cover it above, cutting as it should through the middle.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if the blood flows continuously from above.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open at first, then you must measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign the vessels and cut to the bone.
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	And it should be six centimeters if it is necessary to put the arrow out, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the wound can tolerate, and the closure of the artery.
puis regarde la plaie:	then look at the wound
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	if it remains above the bone point sharp, if the copper that is applied does not come out, then wash the wound and bind it, and the ointment treatment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of the shoulder
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the ancient shoulder dislocation comes, and the cautery is old, due to the moisture of tears and chills in the temples and old age and similar things, and it is treated by methods of medical cures and nothing else helps, then we should strain the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extraction of them is that the hairs of his temples face backwards, and listen to the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well by its pulsation, and is quickly restored afterward in all men who are too fat.
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is restored, then hold his neck with some cloths, then wipe the limb with any rough cloth, and soak the limb in hot water until the artery opens clearly.
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the spatula of which this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then cut it upwards with pincers, and remove all the threads that are adhered to each part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is thin, then bend it to the tip of the needle, then cover that part according to the amount of the two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not covered, it will not heal completely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And draw out some blood from the sixth vein, just enough to reach the third.
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, then it is necessary to tie it in two lengths of a strong silk thread, so that no blood comes before the suppuration of the wound, and comes out with the discharge of blood.
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	then remove the excess that is between the two bones in that same hour, and then, if you see, if he cauterizes with the cauterizing iron directly to the bone as long as the affected parts are removed.
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and this is the difficult work, if the wounds do not have fever and he is of hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cauterizing is to finish the swellings:
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is of greater help against swellings.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	or it is necessary for the extraction of veins that one fills the limb with old cotton and places on well-made bandages;
et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are reset, if there are dry remedies that create heat and tents, until they are healed.
et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if without cutting the artery as much as you work, then you must quickly apply heat with cauterization, or use the glass of vitriol and strain it in your hand that the wound is not soaked.
et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient;	And if you do not have this present, then put salt on the wound as much as you can until the wound is frozen, and raise the limb in cold water until it stops bleeding, and strain it as it should be.
et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And what is more difficult and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cauterization of two parts, but the cutting should be well spaced to last longer without heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When instruments are too tightly fitted, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus;	And it should have between the two knives a space of about an inch, and then when you have marked the two lines, and you melt the hot iron above as far as it comes near to the bone, and cut the vein in two lines.
et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout;	and they should be separated between the two shoulder blades because it is not safe to use this cauterization at all times.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And this is the shape of the cauterization:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis;	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from the veins that are above the skin of the forehead, and it does not profit much from medical treatment, and you see the face of the patient becoming distorted, and it feels as if it is trembling.
et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	and they are kept oiled and moist so that the hair of the papers is burned, and the papers are charred, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is need for this care.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front;	And they call the ancient "curative contusion", and you should do for the back to the evil that has this disease the hairs that it has or front, then make three cuts or front equally according to the length of the front.
et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres;	and it should be one of the cuts just like the second one completely to the front in raising down just above the neck, and the others two on the ribs by above the papers, and guard from the incision of the arteries that are at the two ribs by above the papers;
et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins;	and keep your hand away from the continuation of the lower jaw, and let each wound have a quantity of three drops through the joints.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	and have a sponge piece and wipe the blood off the arrow, then pour the acid of two parts of this is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision;	from the incision which is just above the second incision;
et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	and scrape all that is between the two wounds to the whole face which is above the bone, then make another part of the same incision just below the second, and then extract this acid.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put the instrument called "curette" into the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	and place the sharp edge of the instrument towards the wound and the blunt side towards the bone, and scrape until it reaches the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer;	and cover all the vessels that descend from the head as much as the incision is continued just above the opening of the wound, and then make another part in the same wound just below the other.
et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris;	and then strain out the blood equally, and express the wound for the blood taken;
puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne;	then put in each wound a piece of old linen cloth, and put on bandages soaked in wine and oil and vinegar, and keep away from abscesses.
et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the patient takes off the linen, and is administered a large amount of salt, then the healing ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other remedies to cure wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	renewal of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees;	When anyone comes to cauterize as is customary, and you see the eyes tightened and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers;
et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue;	and the hairs prick, and if they prick in the forehead, it causes great pain and the hairs are discharged.
adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Therefore, treat these accidents with many incisions, and the bleeding that comes from it is like this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the eyelid to turn back, then make a great cut across the eyelid, and another one wide at the edge of the eye.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os;	And begin with the cut on the right temple to the left, and the incision should be just to the bone;
et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier;	and avoid your hand from the nerves of the temples that move at the side;
et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin;	and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood onto a sponge, and then clean between the two lips of the cut and put in thick cotton, and test with linen;
puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut;	Then place bandages soaked in wine and oil above it, and guard against abscess.
quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	When it is broken, it is necessary that you rub the bone until charcoal begins to grow, then treat with things that cause vomiting, which make one vomit.
En teil maniere:	In a similar manner:
pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre;	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of alum, and make a poultice.
et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	and administer it in these wounds to cause vomiting throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses:	All that which drips into our ears is one of the four things:
ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer;	or grains, or beasts, or stones from the mine or similar things such as iron.
ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois;	For seed, as you say, peas, beans;
ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	or liquids that are clear and thin and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it sticks in the ear stone or other kind of thing that does not fit well in the ear, do not let it grow in the ear, if you put the ear to the sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction;	If you see the stone, if there is any drop of purple oil or mustard oil, then moisten extraction.
et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine;	and the patient spits out of condition, and the nose is stopped when the sneezing comes, and puts inside the ear pieces of cloth or wool.
et estent l’oreille au desus.	and the ear is raised up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure;	Many times it comes from this cure.
et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, then moisten extraction with thin prongs, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin;	If she jumps to the pins, it's good.
se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure;	If not, then apply gentle traction at the subtle point of the pin.
et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne;	And if she does not jump by that, then make a hole in the rain and blow her head into the hole or the opening of the ear very hard, and stop up the ear with soft wax so that the rain cannot enter.
puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit;	Then pull it out properly, for many times it comes out like we have said.
et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor;	And if it does not come out in such a way, then take some glue and put it on the teeth, and put something sharp at a point to make it, and put a little cotton around.
puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	Then press the gland above the stone or whatever it is, and draw out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme;	And if she does not spring out of all these things that we have said, then quickly cut the ear as well as the abscess and pus, and spasm;
et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant;	and the manner of the cut is that you first make a small incision in the painful part of the ear, and extract the pus according to its strength, then place the pus between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the grease or fat depends;
et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche;	and let the incision be as wide as a moon, until you reach the stone, then chip it according to your power, and suck it vigorously into your mouth.
et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction;	And if it is small and swells, administer extraction;
et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	and if it cannot come out, administer the following subtle spatula form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that small one.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces;	But do not make it thin when you think the grain is wet due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it.
puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	then extract it with thin forceps and the sucker, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of earwax that falls into the ear, it is necessary to use nasal drops and clear the ear with a lot of old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the very ear itself where the sharp is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out because of the wind, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu;	If not, take many needles according to the length of your thread and thin, and heat them a little in the fire;
et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille;	and insert the hairs one by one through the ear opening, and go up from the other foot, and prick with another needle on top of the one in the ear;
et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer;	and do not stop pricking with needle after needle until the sharp one breaks completely, and thus it will all break off;
et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars;	and if you see, take the reed, and blow one of the needles into the ear, and the other head taken from the fire until the softest reed is burned;
puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	then make another incision at other places until the sharp point is completely out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division;	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, such as a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division.
mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures;	but if it is of large size, where one can feel it, then prepare for the extraction of pins.
et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and if they do not improve, then look at the ear in the sunlight.
s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	If there are no openings, then use fine forceps to pry them apart; and if they do not open, then take the cannula of this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine;	And insert the finest needle into the ear according to the amount of pain, then it forms all over the canal;
fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	Do this often enough until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere;	And if they do not obey to come out, then pack the canal with cotton as I have said in the stone;
et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations;	and if they do not emerge as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have used in the opening of veins, and you will find them where treating distillations;
et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if you drip your oils and your medicines into the ear of this instrument, as you see here:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller;	And if it is of silver or bronze, it should be made with small openings below and larger ones above to drip;
et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton;	And to press during the distillation, use a well-made silver instrument for this, and if you see, take a razor and wrap it around the tip evenly with cotton;
puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille;	Then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the can, and the can should be in the ear;
puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille;	Then push the oil or juice through the razor and around the cotton, and press your hand tightly until the oil is distilled or comes out of the ear;
et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the patient feels the pain within, and sometimes the distilled water is not well heated in the fire as it is poured into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and be careful that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without some kind of ear problem.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	This also happens to adults due to ear wax buildup inside the ear, and this blockage never comes from within the ear if one cannot see it.
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	And never does the blockage come from within the ear, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	That which comes from the front, if one cannot see it, is a painful sensation in many positions, and in this one where one sees, you must put the ear of the bad eye to the sun.
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opacification apparent, if the work has this entire space of from which this is the form:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let it be both and grinding in front and behind all flat, so that it does not blind the ear;
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	if the opacification is of black or of the ear, if you have fine needles, and the coping lightly, until that char is completely crushed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the plug is in the ear, take a thin, light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it on the leather of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the pressure from which the pains are causing pain to hear, lightly pierce, and make sure you do not injure the nerves of the ear;
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	then put a tent according to the width of the puncture, and tie it in the Egyptian knot.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do not do anything until the wound is dry, or take a tent and tie it in a tight rose, and pour powder on top of broken glass.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and if you see the ear swelling, it is advisable to remove the tent and move another tent tied in a hard shell made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood comes out, soak an sponge and wet it with cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood which are either treating the distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper's charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the book that comes in papers of the eyes when they are wet and are dry, if you must extend them with forceps and pins, and the cope of a span of their roots;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	then put it on the broken glass leg.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without peeling, then cauterize with the fine lens burner, and the cauterizer after the incision is good for use;
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	and often they are repaired, but nothing remains of their roots;
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return again.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Frequently arrive in papers things that seem to be crumbled in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail", and it is a collection of large moisture above and below the paper.
li ovraiges est telz:	The work is such as:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	If the hail moves from one side to another, and it is a light thing to know.
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make the wound wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take them with pincers, and cover.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you do not cover it without pricking a little the paper, it will not hurt the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	and if its tear is large, it gathers at a seam, and the treatment until it is healed.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	and if it is small, do not apply force, for the swelling will restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the grain is falling down into the inner part of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the grain in some tweezers, and cover and press from one side and the other;
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is displaced by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the grain is covered, pour warm salted oil on the wound and treat the limb of what causes pain until the injuries are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is smeared on strips of paper and placed above the eyes, and it has more effect on children than adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they have diarrhea in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears flow to their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this, they lie on their faces and sleep on them, and their papers are placed outside their eyelids, which become moist and swell with the exinach that opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the joint to your touch and feel the extrusion among all.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is such that the painful one puts his head in your hand;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a piece of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount that contains each part, then put it on him.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press from both sides, so that the contents are gathered in the circle;
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then cut in the middle of the moisture with a sharp knife, a wide incision, and not larger than the wound made at the opening of the vein;
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and cut the skin until you reach the contents;
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in many positions comes the contents of the incision, in the shape of a white fat piece.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract the honeycombs from all one piece of cloth between your two hands, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And be careful not to push into the folds, that you do not bring all the spanwise to the oil, that you do not harm it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if it does not open at the beginning of the fold, then slightly twist the fold until it opens.
