puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then gently rub the cloth in hot and cold water, and put on the limb, and spread it out well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who bruise the cloth and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient comes to the healer with an abscess that is not drained, then the healer should apply moistening poultices until he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs are artificially placed in papers other than their natural position, and are awakened, they harm the eyes, and bring about diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and cornea, until it is caused by the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And there are four ways to treat it:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	or by cauterization with fire together, or by medicine called "ague" according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by cauterization, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary for you to place the head of the evil in your right hand, then turn the paper of oil to your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If she is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, then prick her with a needle all along the thread above;
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	and let it be on the edge of the paper or where the hair grows from these hairs, and pull the thread above all the paper, and turn it to the razor;
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs adjusted, all the length covering, from the great arm to the little one;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then pull the thread, and put outside the paper a small cotton and linen tent, then on top of the paper a figure of an envelope, like the belly of a mite, and all around it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you saw raise the paper which is divided into two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if you have a tile that requires a lot of paper, according to how the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make all the space between the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large shoulder joint to the small;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cuts near the hairs in the larger part of the root, then lift the skin in one of the two corners of the wound, then scrape all;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then assemble the two lips to one seam of a needle with all the thread of fine silk, and suck the blood, and let the excess hairs above the two edges at any thing gluing, if you see it done.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	And if not, then do not worry about it, leave the stitches and the threads for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound on the side of the stitches with dry and constricting things, for the paper will stick to the suppuration of the wound and the assembly of it, but the stitches are slowly (as they say) dissolving, and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if there is another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and you should shape the paper into a form that is as similar to the gauze of myrtle, as we have told you, into three layers according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then apply this remedy which is above in equal parts according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or one with a thread, and place it in the shape.
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	And put another thread below the large arm, and the second thread below the small one, and tie them evenly between your two hands.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have sewn, as we have said, then gather the two edges of the wound by stitching, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a poultice and other soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and never occurs that the hair of the paper is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if you must use what we have said about incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you convert the paper and make incisions inside according to what I have said, then make two wounds by art, and two stitches as thin as the paper and the width of the space is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and tie them with the two threads where you hold the thread;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble them subtly above what surmounts the paper of the oil, and strain the two wounds from the two parts formed;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and let it remain thus for several days, and the skin that is stretched will die, rot, and putrefy, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, then if the skin has some strength, then heal it until it is healthy.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is covered, and if it is lifted up, the hairs will not grow back.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two needles that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The needles are such that you hold a thin needle, and pull the silk thread soft and thin;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then gently gather the bones and pull them apart slightly, and let the long hairs grow a span long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then order in the hunt another thin silk thread quickly, and pull the main thread tightly.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the misaligned joints on your healthy side.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	Then place it in the sun so that the work is straight and even, then gently push the needle through the entire hunt at the base of the pricked hair, and pierce into the paper firmly until you remove it above the natural hair.
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then pull the hair up to the hunt, and push in the hunt that hair, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then strain your hand until the hairs grow out far enough to cover the entire fur with natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the fur is treated and the hairs do not grow out far enough, then treat the fur with the discharge above until it is completely dry and you can see through the oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Therefore, treat the fur and the thread, close the oil and leave it to dry for two or three days until the hair is in its natural place and grows again.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hairs are small, accompany them with long hair from wild animals, and stretch them out with the one you leave until they are stretched and then tie them.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the preparation of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "porridge", comes in the eye, there are two methods:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by the wound, or by the barber or the cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the method of the work is that you cut out that stitching, and dry the lips from it, and put in tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed;
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and you should only use things that dry and restrict in its care.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I work with things that are softening, such as fenugreek;
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the herbs of high or high and seed of linen be cooked, and ointments of yellow sulfur melted in any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a tent, and the cure for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your cure are such that you must be careful that it does not soil itself according to the form it was before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	and these works that we have said are not other than in order to prevent this disease from returning according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the ear
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidents come from wound and cutting and cauterization and similar things;
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the method of the work in this way is that you hold a needle, in which it has one thread doubled, and the thread in the needle, and you make it pierce from the right arm to the left, so that the thread comes out in two pieces from the needle;
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	then the needle is above all the thread, and the coping is at one span wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what it should be, it is good;
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	if not, take the razor and put it in the groove, and turn the paper, and make two cuts where it costs inside the paper;
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the two cuts of the two angles of the incision that you have made be such that when they are assembled, the figure is as if it were the figure of a letter with no "Greek".
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then remove that char, according to the amount that its cost is damaged from what it should be, from which the paper is made, then add the two parts that are missing, and the cuts of a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the care of what we have said about the softening medicines and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a cut or a stitch or a cauterization, then it is necessary that you make a plain cut outside of the hairs of the papers, and according to what is above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then deviate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	And one should perform the operation according to the form of the disease, as it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters compare all possible methods to how they can make the figure return to its natural shape.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And the wounds themselves, according to what is needed for operation and tools in many different positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The paper is soaked with.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this sewing is done by hand in a certain way that the paper above is smeared with the white of oil, and cannot move or make its natural operations, then it is necessary to bring the tip of a razor outside the paper, and lift it up.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and it is set with pins, until you copy what is airt to the subtle space, which is not too sharp nor too sharp, so that the pain cannot suffer that the subtle space is too sharp and does not burn the oil.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and let your incision, of which you scrape that assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form;
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is healed all that assembly, and never in the sharp salty oil, and lift it from the sharp sweet and with colloid;
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil wool fleece in abundance of urine;
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	and after the third day, use a poultice and dirty things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the joint of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways to treat the joint:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	The first is nerve-related and resembles a hard, dry wound, and the other is not nerve-related but resembles a frozen, white moisture, so that when touched with iron and heated with pincers, it cannot be removed.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Both of them begin near the large bone, and gradually grow larger and larger until they cover the entire eye and all the light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the manner of incision is such that the hairs put their heads in your hand, then you work the eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and lightly hold the paper to your hand, then bend the angle with small tweezers, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put the hair of a horse, or of a sheep, or of a cow, and thread it tightly.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and push it into the angle, and push the needle through the whole, and tie the angle with a thread and stretch it upwards, and scrape all the hair along the side of the needle which leads to the pearl and silk to the hair just above, then cut the remaining in the root of the arm at every subtle thickness and with small forces, and leave the natural skin or the arm, so that by the incision no tears usually come out;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And never has the bone stayed at the joint alone, and over time, as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the skin is all the soft tissue that gives this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the soft tissue does not touch the raw flesh and break it, and that the blood is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	And after the incision, pour in a little bit of bruised silk oil, and make a poultice of charcoal, and leave it just above the other joint.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment that is necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	And if the bone is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the joints cannot enter, often this resemblance of a bone of medicines is cured.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow like I have described in the previous section, and if you see it covered, then work on the bad part, and take a sharp knife lightly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	and you scrape the edge slightly, and if you see that it does not soften and the skin is close, then blow into the oil made of pitch, red wax, and silk thread, and stop the oil on the other side;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then start the other work according to this same work, until it is completely hardened.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk it, and cure the abscess thoroughly until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	and if the appearance of the flesh of the arm is in the oil by great harm, then skim it off and take a part and not all at once, so that no tears come to it;
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	Then pour the red oil of colloquy, which is made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the hair that grows above the eyebrow
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some men are born with no red hair at all, and cover the pearl and hold it above the papers and turn it back, and it seems like a balduster rose.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	And the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand, then they work the hairs, and hold all that hair with suitable bends for this, and support it with strength.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then cut the first hair, and go all cutting to the razor just at the end, and guard that you do not blister the oil in the work.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	and let the incision of the spaniel that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and with small forces of why we remove the skin, as it forms after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	and when the incision is completed and all the char is removed, use silk oil or distilled red vinegar and similar corrosive medicines, and put it on top of the oil with a cotton pad with a cloth soaked in urine, so that it is certain to prevent an abscess from forming.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if nothing remains and the swelling does not subside, and you doubt an abscess is forming, leave the oil and treat the abscess with things that calm it down.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make charms cast in oil by this similarity.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But it is necessary that you strengthen the cure of each weak vein by its natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in ironwork.
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are covered over the eye, and take away from the view their work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	Therefore, the first thing you should look for in that oil is whether it is hot or cold, and there is no other disease besides the first one.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	then the joint should be moved in this way:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	instruct the patient to put his head in your safe place, then gently move the joints all around according to your wisdom, and make the thin bones double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two times per degree in the body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	then move those thin bones gently, and squeeze the blood out hour after hour until you can remove them from the joint:
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	and be careful not to pierce the joint with sharp points of spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not cause harm to those thin bones:
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if you have green and red oil of wormwood to corrupt the humor that remains in the belly.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all the bile in that hour, then make an ointment with the oil of calming things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it stay on for some time until the pain is eased and the risk of abscess is assured, then resume according to this method until they are healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	And that is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The mirror is called "arissati" fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it with fire and medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then make an incision over the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is discovered, and you see the decay and the blackness, if the tool of this is in the form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and it is called "rough chisel", and it is made of iron from the sharp end to the chisel, and it is pointed as a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it on the end of the bone that is decayed, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you know that that decay is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do not do it again, then restore the bone with drying remedies.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the bone is sound, and flesh has grown, and the body of the wound is sound, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not return and is not postponed, and no bad accident happens, then it is healed.
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, there is no other method than to bring the fistula to the opening of the throat according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and you should dislocate the bone the second time with iron and with medicines, and when it is discovered, take the forehead according to this form, and the patient's head of iron at three angles, and the fast should be attenuated just above as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it above the bone of the arm, and keep your hand away from the oil at that point, then turn the whole forehead until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain because if he holds his hand over his neck;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and if the bone of medicines is dry as I have indicated, and when the child is born and the bones harden, then the matter goes to the knee;
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	it is a lighter thing for the joint.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	when the eyes are widely open and do not close due to disturbance or relaxation, then it is necessary to hold the joint.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	then the healthy one, then put suction cups or hatches to draw blood, then put on oil made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply the plaster with bandages and cloths.
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is such that you grasp cloths that are sufficiently soft, and double each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that the wound requires.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then apply pressure from above with a hard bandage, and restart the suctions to draw out without causing injury.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the suctions and leave the oil-soaked bandage on day and night, and if the wound breaks down, it is necessary that you reapply it firmly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the bandage after day and night, and if the oil reappears, it is good.
se ce non;	if not;
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the plasters and bandages and the linen and the leeches until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come in the woven cloth, then it is opened, and comes from far away, like the grain of resin, and is easily seen.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	Therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle into the root of the part desoz jusc’a celi desus, then put another needle where the arm has the double thread of the part.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position;
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then take the limb and fold a double thickness of cloth around it, and tie it tightly, then remove the needle and place some soft oil on the wound.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it there until the thread heals with the wound, then care for the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and never bind the wound with a piece of cloth from each part of a circle, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if they appear to be too large, then pierce the thin sponge that comes with the oil, and wipe away the moisture and dry the wound, and place it immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	then extracted until it is sound.
de la bowe de l’oil	from under the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease, which is called "alcunnati", is nothing more than boil that is gathered in the oil, resembling an acute downward spike, and this is not an acute spike.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit with the bad side elevated and straight, then take the chief between your hands from the two sides, and move it until you see the boil come out above to your eyes;
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	then it should be carefully removed, and not let down and dismantled the light, and see the bad things as they should be.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	and if they do not set it back in place, it is very painful, and if they do not treat it as we have said,
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	if you place the painful part between your hands, then take a fine spatula and make it pass under the transparent skin and the eyelid, until the bone is dislocated.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and when it is out, pour hot honey mixed with melted honey or honey and fenugreek that has been boiled and melted into the eye, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have seen similar cases in the division, and what is needed to pierce it.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	It is necessary that you place the misaligned bone between your crossed hands, away from the light for the sun, and with the sound oil firmly stretched.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then place the paper of the oil on your left hand if the bones are on the left, or on your right hand if the bones are on the right.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand if the bones are on the left, or in your left hand if the bones are on the right, the instrument called "almagda".
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the point of the instrument above the crown by the thickness of a grain in the thinnest part of the oil on the part of the elbow, then strike the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and stretch your hand as long as it pierces through the oil, and feel that almagda is about to reach the empty thing.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	The width of the main vein should be measured from the forehead to the end of the nose.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	And it is the crown of the oil.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the canvas, then put the instrument above it where the sharp is, and press out one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now sharp-sighted, he will see the hairs before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After resting a little, and if the sharp rises again, put the forceps with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not rise, gently turn around your hand back and forth.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	and then place a small needle with a gem, and leave it in the eye until the oil is inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by default the eye is cleaned with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of water, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our household, put on top of the wound with plenty of water.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then pierce only the conjunctiva, and do not move it too much, but make the eye subtle, then push almage, as we have said;
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	and at the completion of the work, compare it to the pain and sleep that occurs, in which it lies on its back in the dark eye;
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and let it be moved in all movements, and take light foods, and do not move its head to the right or left, and let it be tied according to its position just as it is;
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then reset it in the same dark house, and prove its sight, and let it see some things, and then put the joint back just before sunset.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	but it is only necessary to do this at the beginning of the treatment or after the incision now, but it is necessary to gradually increase the height because of the sharp pain.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if abscesses come, then reset the joint before sunset, and give it the food that alleviates the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	and when it is calm, then reset the sight and put it on its face in an orange peel to cover any light, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then slowly go home little by little, and convert yourself to your case;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and remove that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	And some came to us who was of the Iraq, who told us that in some countries they make all people circumcised, because of the acute pain, but never have I seen anyone in our land, nor have I read anywhere in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the similarities of the forms of circumcision, because those who do not know them see them;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and are of pure rain properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they have the same thinness in their heads and the backs in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the head to the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Never born or not issued charred varieties, because there are some that seem like scorpions with many legs;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such and the char is enhanced with a dark color, and if the char has a good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In such cases of these chars that are good, and not enhanced, it is appropriate to make the pain between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and work its nostrils, and pour the oil onto those chars, and the tracks there;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	then hold it in the delicate space under the sharp edge of a part, until you know that that char is completely hardened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there remains any thing that cannot be covered, open it with all the instruments subtly and lightly, so that nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if without causing harm, an abscess forms, treat it as it should be.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize them until the wound is clean and all the pus is removed, then pour or inject hot and sour wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the wound does not open, and moisture comes to the brain, treat it as if it is healthy.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, treat it as if there is bone underneath, because the instruments do not come to cut.
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	then you should go and get a piece of thin linen cloth, and be careful not to tear it with your hands, and have between each thread some space or less.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the hairs of the one you are treating into the linen cloth at the mouth, and pull it out until it comes through the throat.
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often do this with children in schools, and it is an easy thing for someone who wants to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	then hold the head that comes out through the throat in one hand, and the other head that comes out through the mouth in the other hand, and squeeze them alternately as we do with threads.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you have cleaned out that wound so that the new flesh is not corrupted by that char, then remove the thread, suck the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back in its place as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this for three days or more, until the wound is cleansed of all that remains of the char.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Then apply a piece of raw flesh for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for other remedies, use them.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And this is the form of the instrument used to purge the shoulder, with which one distills oils and remedies onto it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And whether it is of silver or tin, resembling an open lamp, like a dog, and conduct it thus;
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	and if you see, then make a closed dog, and let the instruments be played to remove the head;
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	and hold it at the head for when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the head to the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times a disease is born at the head of the nose that is called "tulli", and it grows and becomes large, until it is seen to be a thing to look at;
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore it is necessary that you cut the nose at the beginning, and then open the whole thing, then put the fire cautery or the burning medicine on it;
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if they are slow to cover it until it is large, take note if it is hard, of poor color, and without sense.
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if they do not touch it with iron for it is an infected abscess, for when it is covered, great harm comes to the wound;
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if the abscess is softly touched, not of poor color, and you see that it can be entirely covered, then wash the wound and cover it with things that are secure and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	there are many solutions that come in one of these cartilaginous parts, which is only slightly beneficial to some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Therefore, if there is any, then look to see if the wound is fresh at all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply the two lips to a seam, then treat it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already decayed on one side and the other, then you must scrape all the parts of them until they heal, then gather the two lips to a seam, strain it, and powder with dragon's blood powder and frankincense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	and place the powders on a piece of strong or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it heals through it, then treat the wound with an ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the stitching is such that you gather the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or with needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	In some people there are abscesses within the lips, similar to small or large grains;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore it is necessary to turn the lips, and cut open each one, and take out the pus with forceps and clean every part.
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then apply the wound with a solution of vinegar after the incision, until it is no longer moist.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a dry cloth to the wound, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times, a tooth abscess arises above the gums, which the ancients called "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	If it is necessary, you must support it with forceps at its root, and let the pus or blood flow out.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	Then apply a broken piece of glass or other astringent and desiccating powders to the limb.
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	And if that abscess returns after incision, and often does, then apply forceps again and cauterize it.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return after the cautery;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are gathered at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scrapes that are ugly and sharp;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are the black and yellow and green teeth, until the corruption comes to the gum, and are the stinking teeth;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you remove the pain between your hands, and its roots are in your holy place, and cut the teeth or scrapes that are apparent, until nothing remains;
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	And thus make of the black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are cleaned.
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if one has removed what is at the first layer, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	If not, start again from the second day and the third, until you have removed everything.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	And soak the teeth with various instruments to remove, according to what the work demonstrates, because the razor that one uses to remove the teeth has different forms than the one used between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	And these forms and others be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	It is necessary when you are treating a tooth for pain that you delay pulling it as long as possible, because one should not do this to anyone.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a very high substance that we do not have an excuse for removing.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is forced to be drawn, you should be certain of the tooth's root.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain of the misaligned joint is relieved, and one should ensure that it is a holy tooth, and have the good tooth pulled.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and in any case do not remove the pain by this means, until the bad ones are removed, for we have already done this to these saints.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain of the tooth that is decaying, it is necessary that you burn around the tooth on all sides. with great heat to protect the gum from all parts;
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then move the joint gently with your fingers or thin needles at the first point and point, until it is well dislocated, then firmly fix the needles.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and let the joint with great pain between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not jump back, take one of these tools and push it gently into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the joint is dense and painful, then it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the punctures are.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if the thin needles are firmly held, so that they do not break when being pulled out.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And it is necessary to carefully wipe around the gum to cleanse the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and again give the pain by the greater evil of the root more severe pain from the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be warned that you do not act in such a manner as the ignorant saint does, who through their haste and boldness break everything at once, and never bring back what we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring forth always by the skilled hand of healing for the roots that they delay, or for the cart that they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the mouth with wine or wheat bran and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if blood comes out and often does, use the mouth with broken glass wine.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	If it does not heal, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of the instruments, with which one moves the first tooth, should be long points and large pliers, so they do not double over when you pull the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	These are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick enough so they do not bend when you pull, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have sharp teeth to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the tooth, it is necessary to place cotton moistened with oil or honey on the gum until the gum is softened, then pull out the hooks called "algefri," of which the patient seems like a beak;
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	and they should be made inside as well as a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, it is necessary that you scrape around the root entirely, and there you put the instrument called "althali", which is a spoon, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And if it is also large, so that it does not break immediately, and if its root jumps upwards, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, with all the instruments, because of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other forceps that are before in the range of the teeth, and with this instrument that seems like large needles, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And if these instruments also do not break it, and they are very dense.
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	And so with other instruments, which are not counted as such:
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And the wise masters find their own instrument, according to what their observations and the disease show, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument for the variety of them and if it does not break the cartilage or other bones, or if it hurts, if he looks for instruments that are necessary, as I have said, and helps with gestures, because of which these forms come after:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let the bones be large and well-holding to hold the bone, that it not slip, but that it can be held and removed;
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	and then restore the limb to its proper position, and if it has decay in the bone, and it is small, then the surgeon uses this tool:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not in its natural position, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, then it is necessary to remove the tooth after the decay, and it is not in the right place, and no one can be a dentist or liar:
adonques lou raie;	therefore the rake;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this tool that has such a shape, and it is similar to a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharp at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper is slowly and slowly placed in the mouth for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the copper is removed with a small force as follows:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the tip of the needle with which we make arrows;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in the tip of the tooth, lightly and gradually, so that it does not move until it pierces;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the flat at the end has no razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they are pulling teeth
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the tooth is broken or by percussion or falling, and the pain cannot be relieved by pressing on the gums to prevent it from decaying, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, and this does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they need to be restricted with a gold thread, because the silver thread becomes green and rots, but the gold never does;
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be of a suitable thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth;
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see that the teeth are coming together, then take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the broken ones between the healthy teeth on the other side, as long as you can see clearly into the healthy tooth on the other side;
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then reapply the bandage to the part where you initially applied it, and gently and carefully stretch your hand until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and your bandage should be tied at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the threads with scissors, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the tongue so that it does not bleed on the tongue.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	Then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it stays and serves in this way for the rest of its life, and it is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of two healthy teeth, and two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth is knocked out, if it is put back into its place, little by little, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and does not interfere with it, which is wise and painful, and once made, the shape of a goat's bone tooth is formed, and it is put back into its place where the defect is, and it is held as we have said, and it is left in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut through the cartilage of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	No such thing exists that comes out of the tongue or naturally, which is born thus;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a wound;
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the operations are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and put their head in your own, and relieve the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then copiously lubricate the affected nerve with oil, as long as the tongue is displaced from its position, and if there is hardness or no movement, and it is due to a wound, then apply the ointment and lubricate it generously.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	And be careful not to cut too deeply, as there is an artery nearby.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	And when you have done so, lift the limb with a cloth of red or cool linen, then place a tent over the tongue.
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And apply ointment to the wound every night, so that the limb cannot become infected.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if blood comes out, put some vinegar on the wound.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	And if the blood does not stop, then cauterize with a slow-burning iron, which is good for the body.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then apply other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	And if you see that the wound is of a dark or black color and hard, and if it does not hurt, do not touch it, for it is an ulcer.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	And if it is inclined to bleed and there is moisture, then pour the wound with a thin, sharp instrument, and deliver it from both sides.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it does not remain in place, put on vinegar-soaked cloth until it is cleaned, then return to your work until you remove all the force.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from its socket and shake it, and treat other wounds until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never come from within the throat, which are called "godath", and they are properly called the second mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if they are abscesses difficult to feel and of small size and dark color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with a little iron, as for the escape of blood.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it remain until it is ripe, and then you will break it, or it will break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of white color and the root is thin, have prepared the instrument to cover, but first see if the abscesses are closed and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then place the pain in front of the sun, and its head is in your hand, and the work the mouth and the prick the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue out of all the instrument, from which is the shape.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of silver or fine brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	and you can press the tongue with this tool, and you see the abscess, then take the needle and poke it into the amber, and draw it up as high as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and take nothing from the cloth with it, then wrap it around the tool, of which this is the shape, which resembles a forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and the teeth are sharp, and one side is pointed, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or brass;
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, use a pair of tweezers, which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And it should be chiseled on one side, and on the other part, not;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have cut the one of the arrowheads, then cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cool water, and if there is blood flowing, gargle the sharp pain with hot water, or use pounded green pomegranate skins, or similar things, until the wound is clean.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it until it is healed.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And never do any other abscesses come out in the throat except the two arrowheads, so cut them then like the two arrowheads must be.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged within her throat, specifically a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the condition that was choking her, and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she continued in such a way for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had already been drained twice through both nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore acted quickly, and pushed it in one incision, then cut out the rest, and cut out a large portion of blood.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then I carefully pushed it through the other incision made in the throat, and the work of the mouth and pressed her tongue.
