aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After I applied the bandage to these wounds, and drank a small amount of blood,
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the woman's throat was dislocated, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting into that wound with a long knife;
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the wounds reclosed and filled the skin that I had emptied, until it became very large;
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	therefore I pressed it and cauterized it inside her throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	and it did not grow larger;
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened after that.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When returning to the eye, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is not very large and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help much, and you see that the patient's pain is relieved, and it is thin, then you must remove it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And the one that is round and not very long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	And it is bloody or of a dark color or black, then you must avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in pricking it.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its breadth and length, you should make the hairs sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then cut the cord in the wound, and pull it out, and cover it with one or two of the instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two mandrakes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural end;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cover more, it causes pain to the voice and speech.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the second mandible, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pains are too great for the patient to bear, then it is necessary to use a cauterizing instrument to relieve the pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And if the hairs put their head in your healthy hand, and then press the tongue against the instrument that we have said or in the chapter of cautery, and knead with a sharp, live chisel, so that it is not too thick or too clear;
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and in using the movement of this instrument, because of which this is its shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And it has a head or hair where one puts the medicine, like the movement of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine over the tongue;
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the hairs should lie flat on his chest, so that the saliva and muscle tissue from his mouth can flow into the medicine within, so it does not drip down his throat and into his lungs.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it against the eye for a quarter of an hour, until you see the needle and the medication's effects are eased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and blow the instrument through the entire length of the cotton into the eye until the cotton becomes red.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry and scab after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you are skilled in restarting the cautery of the medicine, then restart it, and after the cautery, apply a poultice of butter around the eye, and clean what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be sure to use cold sharp ones, and treat with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This cure is more saving of the incision, than only the cautery;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather all or some of them in one pot, and put vinegar in it, and make it boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and let the pots be well glued with strong earth, and within the pot has an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the spikes should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the steam rises to the wound through the gum, until the wound is dead.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After the remedy is repeated often, until the wound dries, and make sure you do not apply this at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, for many things happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not apply it until the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	If this instrument is not present, take a knife and place it inside the head, so that the tongue does not protrude too much.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the knife does not cause excessive steam to burden the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Often it is asserted at the throat of bones or spines of fish, or nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore, you must remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all times with the instrument, so that you can see the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	And what you cannot see and is pushed back into the throat, it is necessary that you make him vomit the thing as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	If by chance, the other thing is also dislodged by vomiting.
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the hairs swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a leaf of lettuce, or some dry bread crumbs.
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and ties it to the sponge with thread, and then swallows it again.
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes back up, it will harden, and then be pulled out.
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, take the instrument of a spoon in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised high.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that it does not come out, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and move your hand so the hairs do not push the instrument, for it is better that the hair is out or the thing is clear;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the pushing goes down, or it pulls to all the instrument evenly, as long as it is even.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's lining
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No one has been healed by the saliva, as I said in the division, by the care of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not help much, then look at the throat of the hairs in the sun, then you press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the shoe, if it is made with all small nails, or with thin tongs that are worth a penny.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth a penny, take a hair rope, and beat the evil one in the throat with it, then beat or move the iron as often as you can.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the evil ones are all tired during the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full I of sharp cold, and open the mouth, and the spit out in the direction to swallow, and move it with your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if soon as he feels the sharpness, he spits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	and if it does not spit as we have said, then fumigate the bad smell of putrefaction, with the instrument that I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye;
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, because it will disappear without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of the fumigation is that you hold the pot where he has charcoal visible, and it is covered with a cloth perforated in the middle, and in that punctured place is the object;
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you should give your fumigation, and the painful one puts the head of the snake in its mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes just to the nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the nose will now drip, and if it does not drip, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and suffer the painful one thirst, and give it salty and bitter things to drink, and do not let it drink any sour thing.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it has the task to be cured by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the nose, so it is, when one can see it, similar to curved needles for threading through the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it resembles the beak of a bird, and it has a roughness of lime, so that whatever it takes in, it cannot wear out.
et vez ci la forme:	and it looks like this shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many types of abscesses, according to what memory brings from one and the other in this book, and they differ in puncture and cut.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is in two ways that one is in its own likeness, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those who are at the neck.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those at the base, and the abscesses of the neck are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if to abscesses one should not puncture, until the hole is completed according to its fulfillment.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if they have such that it is necessary to pierce when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by, perhaps because the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which it is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	And if the abscess is beyond the main member, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, it will harm the main member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	And if it is beyond the foundation, then pierce it when it is dead.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And it is not necessary to pierce abscesses that are ripe before digestion is completed, except for those beyond the foundation, which should not be opened until it is ready, and then they will become long and there will be a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	and it is best to lance the pus from the abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and swelling, and the decrease in debility and alleviation of the main symptom of the abscess, and the others;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is best to make an incision lower down on the limb of the abscess where the pus is most dependent and open;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the incision should be made along the long axis of the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all these places equally, where there is no blood flow.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the throat, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it before the sky, so it would flow along with the blood of it, and is plainly full of much dirt;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and perhaps harden the lips and the deeply pierced ones of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pierced according to the wide vein, as the member has need of it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you heal them in small abscesses, small pustules;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many wounds according to the resemblance of the greatness of the abscess;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if at such abscesses or it is necessary to cover the wound, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it has become just as the cloths, and is softened, then it is necessary to do as one does with boils:
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	And if there are such as are cut into three angles, and if there are such as are coped with as the sole of a shoe, as abscesses;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are such as have a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, as with a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce clearly through.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has a great deal of pus, and you pierce, not to draw out all the pus in that hour, but to draw out a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then apply a poultice to the abscess on the other side, then take away anything directly.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times with great pressure, until the wound is completely closed.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	even if the wounds are of weak virtue, or if a woman is carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the patient should never be raised too high with the release of the bow, for by chance the patient may die from the pain, and you would not be blamed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, then suck the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a gaping wound, then soothe the pain with linen or old cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if they are large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you make incisions in each one so that they face each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have pierced into the abscess a part of the skin, and you have pulled it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shredded linen against moisture, and tie it just above the wound;
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the healing ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flows from your work, apply sharp cold and cooling ointment, and wipe the wound, and place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	and if the bleeding persists, and is treated with government and care, and the powders that I have said in hand are in this book, and if it is where it is tense, and if the abscesses are very painful, it is necessary that you put on tents and moistened cloths with vinegar and oil;
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	If the joint is already in this state, and the limb is charred, then it is necessary to apply moistened cloths with vinegar and oil, or wine and oiled, just as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then drain the abscess and dress it, and treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to know generally about the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and read this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the body, and there are ways that are in cloths, such as the lancing of a boil, and very many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are fat and such as have moisture like chickens;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And for those who are hard and bony to cutting, and there is no doubt if the artery is not cut against.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the belly is such that you try all instruments called "intromissions", from which the form comes after, a thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they make it through above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off the hair that contains that moisture, for it returns when one leaves anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then soak cotton in Egyptian oil, if present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, with vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it just before the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And this will continue until it is removed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin the cotton again, as before, the second day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain for a long time.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess remains large, then apply the following remedy:
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and pour water and skin from all parts, and put all your remedy to draw out the pus.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the arrow makes it worse, then do as I said earlier.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this with an abscess if it is pierced, and cut and treat as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting above an abscess, if it is less painful, for they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if any of these abscesses or wounds do not have pus, and are from the same type of abscess or wound that I copied or treated from an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess as hard, rough, and white, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had done so, they would have made just as bad a wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or near, but those that come at the top of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made as low down as possible, to let out the pus;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscess on the neck, and discharge pus, and inflammation, and sometimes appear elsewhere in the body, and are very painful, and are inflamed together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each bubo is properly within its own side, as with the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the similarities of these scrofula are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and some that are harmful and do not wish to follow health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that one which you see in good disposition at the touchstone, and is similar to the color of the body, and moves from each part and is not connected to the veins or artery or conduit, and is not deeply penetrating.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is necessary that you scrape it from above, and scrape the skin of each part, and place the two lips of the wound together as soon as possible, if you have skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and gradually and slowly, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and is not connected to the spongy tissue or cutting, which the hand does not escape, and does not see too soon, before you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to stop the bleeding, put vinegar or some powders that stop blood into the wound, and press the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it stay until the abscess is calmed down, and soften the wound, and begin to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the wound is clean, return to your work, until you complete it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then consider whether there are any small pustules left, and cut and drain them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is much blood in the root of the pustule, then it is not recommended to cut that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through the wound, without causing harm;
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then apply the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the entire pustule, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and hold them in place, as there is no remaining superfluity due to the size of the pustule.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cover the root of it with a covering, and draw out the core, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those abscesses that are superfluous, pierce where it opens and dies.
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce it in this way as the one previously mentioned, depending on it, then immerse tents with oil and similar things, so that what remains does not corrupt from the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well bandaged, the oil cure is added with charcoal until it is healed.
de squinance	of dizziness
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients said and spoke of the necklace of the throat.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen such a thing in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who are choking, the neck's furrow called "epiglottis" must be avoided;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and it cannot be helped by this, because all the veins and the prime evil are in those who have abscesses in the mouth, or in the throat or in the hands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it outside three circles or four a small cut across, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the throat, not in the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those people are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no cartilage, and the valves are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is not experienced, it is necessary to extend the skin of the neck all around, then cut the throat until it reaches the chin.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And avoid the veins of blood, if you see anything, and then cut the throat, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe at the chin that jumps out through the limb that is broken, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a day.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed for which there is doubt of strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound together, and suture all the way through without the cartilage;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause blisters until they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stiffened, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect has left the body.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore one must remove the epiglottis because the hairs cannot hold it, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and because the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four, and then they commanded to sew the wound and heal, as long as it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady came to the sword, and stabbed herself in her neck, and cut off part of the veins of the neck.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not bled from the vein or the wound, blood flowed from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and healed it so that she was well;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and the young lady did not suffer any other harm than that she could only speak softly, and returned to her usual condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I know that in the sewing of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a grape, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	It occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural, which has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one occurs in two ways, one of which is similar to a boil, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it does not require to be opened except in the one that is small, and the proof and search are made throughout the entire incision.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as I have not grasped it, and it cannot be found in any vein, if the copper, as we copper the bones, and bring it to all its covering, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search well soon, and treat as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	For the fire cautery
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many methods of us are, of which I will say all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is fitting that I tell all the difference that is between us and the other.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that the other is cold and fever-causing, until the bile is passed, and is accomplished by the purgation;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without the nout, there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains the syfac, which is its own sacs and is according to the color of the blood, and begins like a rash, and becomes large.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the section.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the care of a new patient, it is necessary to first examine and try the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as found in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of the inquisition of the abscesses of us is that you grasp or more moist skin than you pierce in the abscess, and turn your fingers gently and gently, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then extract the dislocated bone, and take care not to break it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the wound is bleeding excessively, apply a poultice of the same color as the wound, as I have described for other abscesses.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after extracting the dislocated bone, moisture does not come out, squeeze it to remove the grease, then make a cross incision, and take out the pus with forceps, and lightly scrape off all parts and wash the wound with clean cloth that you take away with the blood.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot remove it cleanly, remove it in pieces until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there is nothing left, it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it takes a little while, and does not bother you, use some corrosive powders on the wound, and close the wound, and apply things to relieve abscesses, and treat other cures until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is large, cut out the two lips of the wound, and treat what causes the infection with charcoal.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if it is bleeding and you have no other option, use the juice of broken glass, and leave it on for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the bleeding of the blood.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to the copper cup that was left out.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See the forms of the instruments inserted, and there are three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	large and medium and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three quarters that are called "awl", and one that is called "barrel", and there are three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to puncture the abscesses of fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are also like the needles that one buys for sewing, and are made of brass, or iron, or silver, and cost as much as those that are yellow, and are more experienced in puncturing the sinuses of fistulas.
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the amount of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of needles are mostly similar, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and there are needles that have two barbs in three ways as well.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and there are needles that have three barbs, and they are also in three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and there are needles that have two barbs, and needles of one barb only, and they are also in three ways.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	all of these are necessary in their own way.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these are sharp, and of such that do not cut more than a part, from which we skin the muscles, because we do not want to cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these intermediaries are the almonds placed in the palms, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	And there are three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And we do not use more than in the joints, such as knees, and arms, and breasts, and shoulders, and similar joints.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make another instrument small, resembling scarabs of pustules, according to this form, with which one pricks blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never put back in place which should have healing contact with the veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never burn the breasts of some men when they begin to be corrupted, until they seem like female breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and keep them inflamed and swollen, and whoever wants to heal them, if it is necessary according to this form of this line .b. until .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing ointment, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and cure it until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	And if the jaw is dislocated downwards, and is twisted due to its size, as it often happens in women, then make a cut into the two ribs above, through two similar wounds;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that the other holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two jaws, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for healing, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if it is not safe, or the incision is not completely made, because the hairs do not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it remain until it has absorbed the remaining and grease, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the hocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the hocks are hard lumps or have ribs, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it there for a day, then remove all the cotton, and treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to pustules, then treat them as we have said about incising pustules, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the skin above it is sound, then often an abscess forms, and similarly, there is often bleeding from the vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if it is known, then one should know when it is for the artery, as the abscess is long and flat.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you sense your duty, if you sense tightness;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then it is necessary to be careful of appearances;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	it is foolish to cover this abscess, and immediately when it is outside of the bones and muscles and where it is very deep, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should avoid the cure of iron, and the one at the head should also be avoided, and in the one that is from the enlargement of an artery made through the long skin;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the incision as small, and then tear away the artery of the webs, until it is exposed;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut off the arrow from one side, and pierce it through to the other side, and stretch the artery with a double-stranded thread according to what I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then puncture the limb that is between the two ligaments of an instrument until the pus that is inside comes out, and remove the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the remedy as I have instructed, until the wound heals.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this condition that has occurred to it, until it is healthy.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is in the belly, it is necessary that you dip your hand into the abscess to remove all the pus from the skin, then pull out the needle away from the limb that you hold in your hand, and pierce it, and if there is a double layer of skin, so that you can draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or with one of two threads from the two wounds.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then insert another needle all along the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and stretch the threads into four loops.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then drain the abscess until the excess pus is removed, then clean the wound and leave what remains.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply a moistened cloth with wine and oil, then treat the wounds with tenting and poultices until they are healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come in the artery and vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And there are often injuries and doubts in all these cases where there are joints, and it is the painful abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is stretched, the patient feels great pain, and it is not in the same position as the flesh, but outside of the wound.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor dislocate nor displace, and that which is in joints does not need to be covered by iron.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance I had contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and that which is at the head or face, makes the skin to the spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take a needle and lance it at its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, hang it from the tip, skin it, then bone it and stitch the wound to the seam, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large tumors hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Never occurs in the abdomen and no other place, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it is in the fine roots, and the large legs.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	And there are small and very large ones.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw a man who had two in his belly that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were torn, and were filled with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I took them and found in one eighteen ounces heavy, and in the other six drachms, and the work of the incision is that you look to see if the roots are moist, and the color of the root is white and moist and of fine root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If the copper is wide at the spout, and they are present with the fire cauterizer.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in cutting, there are often too great losses of blood, and if you do not stop it, then hurry to use the fire cauterizer;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the evil spouting and painful from the cut of the iron, then take a piece of cloth well made, and tie it around the wound as we have said, and leave it for two hours;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then tighten it, and do not stop pulling the cloth from below until it covers the wound, and cut through it with effort.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are large, then it is best to cover them directly on the belly, but you can also cover half of it, then cauterize so it does not return.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and make sure you do not cover the thrush which is of pale color and poor sensation and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is some abscesses which become infected, and I will come to the treatment of wounds after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the foot is injured,
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	if the appearance of the bubo comes from fire wound or cut of syphilitic, and is above the belly and in some of the sores, as it has in other wounds, or of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of moisture;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If it is by the breaking of the tooth and through the discharge of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various sources.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the purpose of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides so that it returns, and then it comes back, and perhaps if it is torn, and expands greatly at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	If it is by moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, but do not force it.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	If it is by blood, it opens with these signs that the abscesses are large and hard, and it is filled with a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by windiness, it is a swelling at the touch, and the work is that you look to see if it appears from the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave, let them care for themselves.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For as I told you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestines or the boil, then it is necessary to command the patient to tint his bandage, and be stretched out straight, then sign all around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have signed all over, then stretch out half of the abscess above all the big bone;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie him around with a strong thread, or a tight silk cord, and let it be loose on the injured limb;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open the half of the abscess stretched out over the limb, and insert your finger, and pull out the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find the joint, pull it out, and push the intestine to the side of the belly.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bone, take it by the end, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein makes you go against it, then go around it, and return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads, and push the two needles around what you have done in order to pierce.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it is healed, and cut the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when you cover it with a thin cloth and pour in what is necessary, then treat the wound as we have said, and drain the abscess.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the arrow or the moisture that you have removed, then treat the limb as it needs, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should treat with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say the chancre is ingrained in the marsh, and great caution in its treatment, and the ancient one said that when chancres are in a place where it can be removed as if chancre which is in the breasts, and in the armpits, and similar places, and all of it must be removed when it is at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	When it is large and old, it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never been able to heal it.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I have never seen any healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the work, when it is in place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you remove the evil of black bile once;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it healthy if it has manifest repletion, then remove the evil from the good limb to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pour your ointments or salves, and hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow fully, and clean the wound well with your hand or something else, and if the blood clots against the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then perform other treatments until they are healed.
de ydropisie	For hydropy, instruct the patient to let the h
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have said in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and how the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment by medicines, and that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only illuminated.
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	And one should not touch iron in these two similar cases:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	That is to say, tympanites and hypospadias, for this is a deadly matter;
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this resemblance of hydropsy which is called "eclites" of medicines, and the cure does not help, look if the pains are weak, or if he has another disease than hydropsy, as in all cases and solution of the belly and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if you do not touch iron, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	And if you see the pain of great virtue, and he has no other disease than hydropsy alone, and he is not too thin nor too old, then thus proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Raise the painful limb up to your hands, and the assistant presses the belly by pushing the sharp instrument to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula with spinous form according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	and the tip, and make sure it is not too sharp so that it does not pierce the intestine when cutting, and it does not bleed;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the hernia is pushed against the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you cut them from the belly three fingers down from the navel;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the hernia is due to the disease of the liver, then cut your incision on the right side of the belly three fingers down.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is for the shoulder, then to the right, and it should only be that the painful parts are shown above the wound so that the excess does not run to the weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and the bone, and loosen your hand to all the space between the skin and the flesh as when scraping at the quantity of an inch or around.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the flesh until the space reaches the wound, and this is the end of the needle, then remove it, and then pierce with this instrument which has the following form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light brass or silver, and has a small hole at one end.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on the other side, three small holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on another side, and one on the other.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is shaped like a quill, and is cut as a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make on the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top of it is the nib, so that when the instrument comes to the tip, they now write with it.
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	Therefore, empty the middle or one-third part, because if you empty it more than necessary at that hour, by chance, it may cause the patient's death due to the resolution of their spirit from the arm, or they may lose their hand, or they may approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of its power, and according to what the arrangements of the power of evil mean, and its fangs.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then take the tool and hold the sharp edge, and it is now held by the one who stops the perforation that is above the puncture, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then restart the tool on the other day, if you see the evil suffering, and take a small quantity from the sharp edge.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do this every day, and be careful not to follow for as long as it does not delay but a little sharp edge.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	If you doubt the injury and leave it for too long, the wound will be covered with dirt or sand, and by much sweat or bathing and in the sun, and it will become infected from drinking.
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And the treatment of drying medicines until it is clean, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born who does not have some pertuss in the rod, or the pertuss is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce very thinly throughout the entire length according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or pierce a thin needle through the bottom, and tie it and keep it thus for three days or four, and when it wants to urinate, if it is removed, and urine is made, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And by chance, it does not seem to fit, for the urine that comes out does not keep it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pierced is small, then treat him with a thin piece of cloth from the bottom, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the perineum in their joint cannot give birth, for none are born with the perineum at the top of the staff, because it cannot urinate before they raise their staff up.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	And they cannot defecate because the matter cannot come out just to the marsh, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the way of the work is such that the pains are hidden so quickly on their back, the top of the staff and the copper as like the waist of a pen, so that the perineum opens in the middle, as it should.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and guard against the flow of blood that often comes, and if it does, if the cloth that stops blood flows, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pus from the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	often come these blisters on the finger, and it is an ugly appearance of a char.
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are both harmful and not harmful ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if it is necessary that you squeeze them at the base, and clean and dry all, then put on gauze in Egyptian bandage;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of bandage until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a malignant ulcer, black and putrid, then you must apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	if you have cleaned it, and if the blister is inside the finger, and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then it is necessary that you remove the blister that is inside first;
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when it is swollen, if the doctor is not present.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you treat it together, if you are not sure about the fracture of the bone that it is not pierced, and then blackness and corruption in its bone and where the connection.
