si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut off all that is black and corrupted, then bind it with the plaster of honey and flour that is made of the skin of grapefruit and cloves, then the doctor of other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	If bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery if helps in two positions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	That is to say, at the drainage of abscess, and at the corruption.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the head of the shoulder is broken and twisted, it is necessary that you break or direct the staff like a club, and urinate on the wounds.
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin is pulled across the head of the staff which has not been circumcised, or it has a wound or an abscess, then you must burn it with the instrument that has hair, until the flesh is separated, and deliver the head of the staff from all parts;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a difficult thing to divide the head, then you must burn it with the spatula at any part of the head and the skin;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	Then thoroughly dry between two and one puts a thin layer of fine flax thread in cold water, that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not different from other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Whenever we perform this work of our will, and properly in children, it is a matter that we should do the best work, and the lightest for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the largest part of masters and sages who performed circumcision during childhood, and with force, and at all one time;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if it was the chosen one because there were two cloths, and perhaps if one covered it from above and delayed the other outside.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	When it is covered with copper, and the pain is doubled, and the wound cleansing which is done from below is not sure of the exact point of the member;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and the cleaning of the finger by chance escapes the iron, and ruins the work, and many times it happens that they do not have to clean it, and I want.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the mundication which is done with force to all the length of the thread, I have found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut as much from above as from below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut evenly in all the skin;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread is well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	and that the method of the first work is such that you make the child think, if he listens, that you only tie the thread around the rod as much as possible, and then throw it in all the ways that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	then place the fetus between your hands straight out, and apply force between your hands or away from your feet so the child does not see it, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	then close your hand around the staff and blow or suck, and pull it up until the desired length of the staff is reached.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	then clean it well of the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it from one end to the other.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and hold it with two fingers of the second hand at the pouch and the index, and pinch between the two ropes, then pull the child up gently and pull out the staff.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for it is the most dangerous.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and apply powder on and on the powder with the glue of a mule's hoof boiled in quicklime tempered with rosewater, confected with rose oil and fresh, and let it stay overnight, and continue the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces at the mummification is as follows:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two forces should be equal and strong, and the forces should also be great like the even hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of mummification is that the cuts are made too deep at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore, you must extend it to your angle, as the joint causes an abscess.
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	And the coping evenly, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then use nails, and then the coping.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they overshoot three times, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess is fully healed, and scrape lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if the coping moves as you can move it, and keep away from the part of the rod, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore cure the limb of soiled wounds from powder, which we have said or treated in the treatment of powders, and if the coping is done too carefully, it goes beyond, it will not harm;
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure the dislocations, as we have said, until they are healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retaining of the urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is caused by the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or a bone, or charcoal, or similar things, as we have said in the section.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone which is lodged in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary to pull it up over the knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And let them be placed on their backs, and extend their belly from the upper part of the back, and restrain the hairs as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and consequently, the neck of the bladder is pressed against the stone above, causing the urine to leak out.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come out as we have said, and the pain is great, then you must administer extraction using an instrument called "syringe", which has this form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it should be made of thin silver wire, like the quill of an eagle.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and it should be the tail of a long and half-palm, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the way to extract urine is that you take a double thread of yarn or cotton, and tie it to the tip of the syringe, and pull the thread inside the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And cope the excess of the cloth and the bottom with juice from the slingshot, then oil the slingshot with oil or butter and egg yolk, and place the painful area on a chair, and apply the wet cotton and oil of olive and vinegar;
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	then lightly place the slingshot in the cotton, until it reaches the base of the cotton, then double the cotton over against the bandage;
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	then press the slingshot before juice from the cotton, and feel the pain coming with the empty thing, and this is not made according to this order unless because of the reason that it leads or goes is twisted;
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then the thread is drawn through all the yarn slowly and slowly, and the urine follows the yarn, then it is extracted forcefully, and make a correction of the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and restart the catheter until the bladder is emptied, and align the hairs.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood enters the bladder, or putrefaction and assembly occurs, and you see it distill water and medicines, then use any tool called «clepsedre», and its form is:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three openings.
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	one on one side, and one on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	and the threads are inserted through the holes that the medicine cuts so that it stops well the urethra, if one can draw out the moisture, and put in what is needed.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	When you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it to the drainage which is inside.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you drain the moisture from the catheter, and then blow strongly into the drainage inside.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moisture enters inside, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	And this is the form of the subtle catheter with which you catheterize the bladder:
si est ci:	It is as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or brass, and it is the highest one.
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	And it is open at the top where the bend is.
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you saw clustered in the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a double thread of wool, and heat the moisture over the fire.
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then push the tip of the cluster into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the hairs feel that that moisture has come to the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	And if you do not have a bladder, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it roundly through.
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then push the thread strongly into those holes, then assemble the circle as you would assemble a bowl, and put inside what you saw of oil and moisture and salt, and tie it in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as you have done with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the previous section the ways of arrows and their extraction together with remedies.
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between an arrow embedded in rain and all the signs, and in which arrow one should make a cut.
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	And in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the arrow that is embedded in the bladder often happens to children, and it is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder resembles a sharp pain in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it opens the hair, and grinds the painful spikes, and does it many times, and then soothes.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and with much of these, the base.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and is light for the healing of children up to four years old, and is very painful in the elderly, and is constant in those between youth and old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is the cure lighter for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with a poultice, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders one from seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the pain by the feet, and stand up and move away from the side, so that the stone descends to the base of the bladder, and does not come out once high.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	then let the patient sit between your hands, and his hands should be away from his thighs, so that the urine flows downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then the knees and the toes;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel a stone in the space, hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not break at the touch of all, then rub your right index finger with oil from your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and place it at its base, and knee the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the foreskin with urine.
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press against your thumb, and the bone against where you see it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and command him to extend the right testicles with his hand, and the left hand remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the cut is made.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then insert the spatula, which is shaped like this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make a cut between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval.
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And the cut should be straight above the stone, and your thumb should be on the fundament, and the cut should be across so that it is wide outside, but narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	If by chance the pressure is too much for what it should be, which is on the foundation, it will suddenly jump out of place.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And it slips that there are stones or sharp edges and margins where it can get stuck.
si est griés a issir;	If it is greasy to pull out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And if there are parts that are soft and smooth like a glove, with a rounded shape, its extraction is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	In this case where there are sharp edges and margins, make the incision wider;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump out, then it is necessary to hold it with forceps that are like a clamp at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping.
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	And if you do not engage it thus, the small pox will spread, and if it is not dissected, then strain it with vinegar.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And if there is more than one stone, first remove the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove it, and the smaller ones later if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or the urine flows out because the sutures cannot hold.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	But if you try to pull it out, or tear it off with pliers, until you tear it into pieces;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bandage it, and place a moist cloth on it soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold rosewater, to alleviate the abscess.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then resolve the pain on its neck, and do not let the bone slip back into place.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, rub the joint well with oil and vinegar, then apply a poultice of mustard plaster and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if the abscess comes to the wound and corrosions, and congelemens of blood in the bladder, and it is retained so that the urine is held back, which is known in a certain way as without a jump with the urine:
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then put your finger on the wound, and remove that blood, because if it remains, it will irritate the bladder, and it will spoil.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound with sharp and smooth and silk, and help in all ways that you can, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the bandages that you use to treat him, that you tie them around both thighs, and place the medicines on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if it is a small stone, and it is conducted with a reed, and tied around, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the cure of which I said before, that you cut many times, and excuse the cutting for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already experienced this.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron rod according to this form and be at three angles tied with a thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the stone outside of the bone, so that it cannot return to the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then gently push the finger into the thread until it reaches the stone.
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	And slowly turn the finger back and forth in the stone until you can pierce it from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	If urine comes out soon, then press your hand above the part of the stone that remains inside the thread.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is already broken and shoots out with the urine, and is sharp on the hairs;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason that defends it, then tie the thread outside of the stone and the other above, then make the thread in the place of the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and release the thread, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healer as long as he is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It rarely happens that a needle is inserted into women, and if it ever does, then the healer is in great distress, and it is prohibited for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	One is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	And the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-informed and willing to reveal her secret, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman who is well-informed in this art of hands.
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth reason is that if the woman's needle is longer than the man's, because it should have a deeper groove and there is great pain. And if necessary, one must send for a woman who is well-informed and knows how to insert the needle, and if you do not find such a woman, then it is not advisable to proceed with the operation.
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And the present one is a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and she commands that she do what you command of the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very closely if the woman is virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to place her hand or foundation and seek the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then she must hold her hand away from her foundation, and recommends that she place her hand or with the pain, and press her right hand firmly on the bladder:
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	if she finds it, then it is necessary to move it from great to great from the entrance of the bladder until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Then cut into the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the knee, where it is moved and feels the stone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his leg above or below the stone, and let the wound be small at first.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	Then stop the bleeding in the wound, if you feel the stone so sharp that the wound can be closed until the stone can be removed, and know that many ways of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	It is to know, small and large and sharp and smooth, long and round, and those that have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you have similar cases to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if you do not know, then put it in vinegar for an hour until the stone is cleaned.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have the tools that I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for people to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it does not move, and it is the artery that is cut, then put powder on the wound and bandage it with tents and bandages, and do not start again, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient dies.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, then return to your work until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Water is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white saphir, which is dissolved out of the cavities that contain the urine.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "syfac", and it is never properly in the web of the eyelid, if one thinks that it is the other eyelid;
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the thick skin between the white syfac that we have said;
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and it does not have a name.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this branch is due to its weakness that comes from the roots, and it is spread by that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And it never comes from striking on the eyelids, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is yellowish to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or watery white, and it has more;
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is the white syfac that we have said, then the abscesses are present, slightly long like the shape of an eyelid, and do not open the eyelids, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if he has moisture in the own bandage, then abscesses are treated with a part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg;
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if his moisture is between the skin of the wounds and the white sfax, then he feels it well;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore when you want to know the color of the moisture, try in all the surrounding tissue where it was before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introducer, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure it with iron, then it is necessary that the hairs be cleansed according to some power and the replenishment of his body;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then the sweat on his back, above something a little high, and put much cloth on him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then lift up on the right side, and command the minister to lean to the left, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the ribs;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cover the ribs with the skin on the long side up to the sharp point, and your blade should be straight in a cutting motion across the ribs towards the white face, and gently scrape the skin according to the power;
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the white face flat with a sharp, wide opening, and extract all the sharpness, then place your forceps, and press the white face upwards;
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the bones of the ribs, but only the sinews.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	and carefully remove the entire or even the ribs themselves, if you do not cut it well, it will return to him sharply.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the bone breaks during your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the sinew.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then sew together the two pieces of the rib bone at a seam, then treat it as with other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	And if you break the bone and it becomes corrupted with another disease, then it is necessary to tie the veins that are suspended, in doubt of the flow of blood.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then copulate the joint to all the suspensory, and strain the eye, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is sharp and assembled in two parts together, these are two branches.
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If you copulate the other part as you have done the first evenly, then soak the blood, and put in the wound linseed steeped in rose oil.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And put on top other linseed steeped in wine and oil, and put over the two joints, and put over doubled cloths, and tie it to all the limb which is according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and place them according to this pattern and sewn together at the waist of the undergarments, and one of them on the back just above the buttocks, and the other at the side where the armpit is.
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two over the two angles, and let the whole assembly be the restriction in the loop of the undergarment.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never apply this cauterization in the form of an iron tail, and it is that you grasp the delicate cauterizing needle and pierce the skin of the wounds, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white matter that contains the acid is discovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Take the fire cautery in this form, and pierce the affected area with a thin needle, and burn the skin with this delicate cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And cover it in all ways that you can, until you remove everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and be careful that the flesh does not touch the bone;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and make sure that this work is more safe;
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and keep from bleeding of blood, and make sure that the work of the needle is even;
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing goes against you, or an abscess forms or bleeding occurs or other things, then cure what goes against you, according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the pain is unbearable, and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then apply perforation as I have told you, and when you are certain that the boiling water is ready, place the injured part on a raised seat.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess in the unaffected part of the body, and place the perforation at a distance from the entire length of the body.
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	And let the holes be wide enough so that all the sharp pain is removed.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then place cotton on the wound and tie it, and let it bleed until all the sharp pain is removed, then care for the wound until the wound is healed.
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not allow the sharp edge to exit from the mouth of the wound, then you should insert a pen or the instrument used to treat hydrophobia, of which the form is as follows:
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and widen the wound slightly, and make sure that the sharp edge returns, and it is reassembled after six months or within a year, and when it is reassembled as before, and thus it will pass the pains in its course.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	make sure that in the section of this branch, many positions are possible, for which it seems to me that moving it is better than leaving it;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I will tell you about the work and similar things of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	Therefore, many abscesses come from wounds, and at the same time from blows;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive sharp and wet, which is expanded from blows, or from impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess according to the color of the blood;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and does not show pain, and is a painful abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And perhaps some gray, painless and pale abscesses, and of yellowish color, and never come from a vein or from inflammation of the blood.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is by the out of artery, then it is known by the position of the abscess being high, when you press it to your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it only requires that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	Those who are made of venous blood are known by their position at the expression of gentle touch of the fingers, and can well do the cut across this resemblance, and across others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and it is that you cope the courage of the coins, then the wound is high, and the trauma from the white swab, and deliver the suspended part of all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the shoulder is already set with these charms, then it is necessary to remove the shoulder and the cloth.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is in the armpit or inside the ribs, then it is necessary to remove all of that which is inside the ribs, and the cloth should be replaced.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the hair at birth is on the back of the head, it is necessary that you shave it all, and straighten the forehead, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply the wound with a soft cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then apply other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess surrounded by an envelope resembling a blister, with the softening of the sinews, and the painful movement of the limbs as it moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this disease is just as difficult and painful as the previous one, and we will tell you about it in the work, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	You should sit the painful limb on an elevated seat, then lift the suspensory ligament of the fingers to your two fingers, and all the tendons that are close to the carpus, and comb the masters, and extend them properly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut the sharp spatula wide through the tendons at that place, as long as they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then insert a needle or one with double thread, and tie it to the first joint where the blood came out, and tie it to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then place the copper correctly in the middle, according to the length of the wound, and draw out the corrupted moisture;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others by injecting ointment, so that no one notices that they have inserted one of the coins.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for if there is no harm, and all the men come in sight, then it is necessary to remove the coins from all the men.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	if they do not lose their coin through the incision of the men, and dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The consequences of this branch are due to the section that comes or sticks out, or the extension over the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that break to one of the coins.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	And this rent is due to either too much sucking, or from the extension of the limb, and these two methods come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from impact, or from jumping, or from a loud noise, or from lifting heavy weight, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is due to too much sucking, is that it happens slowly and gradually, in a long stretch, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are even up to the chest, because the sucking quickly reaches the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs of the cutting of the tongue are that it brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and there are various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart because of the cutting of the tongue.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the misalignment, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron with fear, because it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of treatment is that you command or prick at the intestines to twist them into a ball in the wound, if it can be pushed back inside;
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	Then place it on its shoulder. Between your hands, and lift the elbows;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then press the chest above, and cover all the skin of the ribs;
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then stuff between the buttocks woolen cloths according to what you have skill to open the wound, and let them be such that the eyes do not come out;
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then scrape the belly that is outside the skin of the ribs, until the white belly is exposed from all parts;
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then stuff your middle finger in the part that leads to the ribs, in the part between the white belly that is outside the skin of the gut, and between the second belly, and depart from where it is behind the gut, and between the second belly;
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and if it moves to the right within the curve of the ribs, and places the white cheek on your right hand, and raises the chin towards all the face towards the waist;
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and commands the assistant to extend the chin upwards, and release what is behind the jawbone;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and ask if there is any intestine wrapped or white cheek hard, and if you find anything, if it pushes against the belly outside;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle or it has the thick thread made of silk, and push it into the back part of the face, which is after the skin of the ribs;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	After the belly, then cut the tendons that appear like hairs, as long as there are four hairs.
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	Then gather them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and bind them with a strong thread of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then wrap the tendons like hairs, and bind them with two parts of thread, so that no one who might touch them could enter into wounds, as an abscess does not come.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And then apply the thread along the first thread of two parts of that, and after these two threads leave the thread that is outside the skin of the belly, the great one of a dowry.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	and then the other according to the roundness that the mouth carries.
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	then cut in the part that is outside the skin of the fingers, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply a softened wool in oil to the wounds, and put it on as we have said before.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white, pus-filled wound that we have said, after incision, due to doubt of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	for this has often been done, and leave the wool until it heals over it.
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it takes too long to heal, then boil water and put it on as we have said before until it heals.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with other treatments until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to make the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made so that it is like a branch that is together with the bone, in a way that you tie the vessels, after the incision slightly to the outside.
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	Then cover it with a bandage, and treat the abscess that works, until the vessels die.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment as we have said, until they are healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	No time comes for tearing and breaking, as we have said, and open the veins;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not cut any of the intestines at the same time, and if there is, it is little, and repair every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	And if he remains too long at this point, the wound or the infection spreads, as the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And it happens by the extension of the pus that is in the angles, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and the muscles are stretched and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	And the treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously said.
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And it is never treated in this way:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	And the hairs are cut off with a sharp blade over their back between your hands, then the limb is stretched widely according to the quantity of three fingers.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and then extract the sinew that is outside the skin that connects, then take the tendon and put it on top of the bone that appears from the sinew.
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it against the front of the abdomen, then cut the two bones that appear from the sinew above the head of the tendon, and cut both.
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the head of the tendon, and do not cover it with the sinew or extend the wound or anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the root of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	then treat it according to the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you remove the splinters, uncover and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The splinter is hidden, and does not appear in the rent, and the cauteries are dull in this limb, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of leather from harnesses
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times the tendons of the joints are softened in some men, because the cartilage inside is softened and it can be seen.
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	and it is a matter of skill, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the misaligned part lie on its back, and the copper which is softened over the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	then join the two lips at a seam, and if you see that it is too much, cut off the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches;
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	then cover between the seams, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and cut off the thread.
dou chastrement	for gently
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	It is said that these things are not mentioned in our law, and for this reason I do not want to speak of them in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and are necessary for two ways:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one is that the physician responds when asked, and in his knowledge the cure;
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have experience in castrating some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and rams and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by traction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we make by traction, we make our seat the animal in high heat, until the testicles are softened and during;
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then hold them in your hand, until they are reset and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille:	The punishment of the waist:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	it is necessary that you rub the animal skin with your right hand, and press the leather of the sleeves against it, then tie the suspenders, and burn each eyelet at the top, when you have well scorched them;
et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz;	and leave no spot of the face and the subtle face that is on the sleeves;
et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this method of punishment is better than that which is made by attraction, because at the attraction something remains from the sleeves, by which the animal desires pleasure;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	There are two main methods for men:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	One method is that between the two testicles, open wide as the natural shape of a woman, with hair and sometimes cutting the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has a penis like a finger and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of men and women is that you remove all infected sores, and treat them as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second method, men whose urine sprays through the skin of the testicles have no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the incision
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tenting is an infected sore above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see.
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	and some women have had it as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	You should wipe away the excess blood from your hand or fingers, and clean it lightly.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do not move too much in front, as arrows do not come, then the treatment of other cures until it is healed.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and another char that is born from the mouth of a marsh, and use it, and by chance it jumps forward, and it is similar to a cow, and for this reason they called the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to treat it, as we have said about the treatment, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	It is erratic when the nature of the woman is not well known, or the pustules are small.
et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est;	And it is either natural by birth, or an accident due to disease that has come.
ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or it is due to a charm, or a subtle blow or sharp, and it is done by force in the marsh, or in the ribs, or outside, or wherever it may be.
et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir;	And they prevent the conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have.
et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	And the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the tail.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears to be nearby, then it is either yours or his.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi:	If it is a subtle blow, and it is near to the two lips, then you hurry, and the treatment will be as follows:
met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes;	Put your two index fingers together, and the woman is on her back, spreading her legs;
puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens;	then the two books are formed, as long as the subtle sphincter is not torn, and not over the obstructions.
puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	then take linen, and soak it in oil, and place it on the limb, and grind the woman against him every day, so that he cannot stitch.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the facial swelling is hard and rough, then it is necessary to apply a poultice like a leaf of mint.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope;	If the obstructions are made of bone, then soak it in vinegar and cover it.
et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef;	and have the remedies stained with blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and plenty of sulfur.
puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder;	then apply a wide piece of cloth, so that the wound cannot stitch.
et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec;	and then let it be long, and the bandage a tent of dry linen;
puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes a horse's kick, cover it according to this method, unless it is an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the infected abscess in the marsh, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Emorrhages are openings of veins which do not usually bleed, and when the emorrhages are old they become thrombosis.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	and we have had in the section similar cases and signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thelul, when they are formed in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, if not treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh, are those that can be treated.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses;	Therefore it is necessary that you put the woman in a cool house, then apply leeches, and the cope in its roots, then powder of medicines restraining blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things.
puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide;	Then, press his feet against the wall for an hour, then put it in cold water.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	And if blood comes out, if it sits in a decoction of sumac and the skin of green apples and galls and similar things, then take flour of wheat, mix with honey and egg, and make a poultice on his back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If he is strong, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir;	If not, then make him dizzy by suction at the back and breasts without hurting;
puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	Then take the cloth, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elder with old wine, and make him dizzy at the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when the abscess is ready, treat the wound with poultices until it is healed.
et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul;	and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the sharp chief, so cover it as I have said for the throat.
et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses in the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscesses come in the marsh, such as chancre and pustular abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and chaut abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe;	Therefore, I must say in this treatment of the abscess that comes in the marsh, which is not one of the abscesses that are filled with pus.
et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	And if you know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is hard and at the beginning of its arrival, and painful and feverish, and if it becomes red, then you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie;	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but wait until the pain is eased;
et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe;	and then place the dislocated part on the seat, and have two small seats where it leans, and support it on its back and gather its feet to the sides of the leg;
et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien;	and let its knees be spread apart, and place its arms away from its hips, and tie them together with a strong cord;
puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme;	then place the ball against the right side, and introduce the tool used to make the mouth of the marsh, from which afterwards comes the form;
et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide;	and it is necessary that when you see this tool being introduced, that you check the depth of the marsh, so that nothing comes in front of it which it should not, and that it does not dislocate the limb;
et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve;	and if the instruments are larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the marsh with cloths, so that the instruments do not hurt him.
et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	and it is necessary to put the horn of the instrument above, and to stain the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit;	And when the abscesses are open, and they make it by hand, then it is necessary to cover the head, at the spatula level.
et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec;	And when the wound is drained, then it is necessary to put in the wound moistened cloths in red or green dry oil.
et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites;	and put the bandage of the wound at the depth of the marsh, and put above the marsh and above the clean moistened cloth in vinegar or wine.
puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the healer after two hours of heating comes to the patient, as long as they are healthy.
et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites;	and never lift the marsh and the wound with a poultice of honey and honey, and then with honey or roots of lily and aristolochia being cooked.
puis reveigne a l’oignement.	then reapply the heating.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is sutured with a marl, it is necessary to be careful not to use iron, but to cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar:	Midwifery is first to the birth that she knows the natural shape of the child, and the signs if it is when you see the woman approaching, and wants to smell the armpit.
adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir;	then quickly take the child out.
adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui;	then shake that child according to its natural shape, and it comes out with its head first, and the second part with it.
et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost;	and when you see these signs, if it is necessary to gently press on its belly, so that the child comes out quickly.
car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification;	for when it descends with its head first, and the second part is with it, and it is cleaned of its excess by good washing.
et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	and this that comes differently does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises;	for it never comes out of its feet, and it comes out forcefully from the back or the head, and the hands, or it comes out over its belly, or sometimes, and it is turned by chance on its neck, and by other bad shapes.
si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	If it is necessary for the shoulder to be skillful and subtle in these things, and if one becomes aware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent;	If the child comes out through its own head, and the woman gives birth painfully, and the strength of the one who is giving birth is weak, then let her sit on a seat, or the women hold her.
et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	And take oil or fenugreek cooked in its own fat, and then give the shoulder between its two fingers the smallest amount of it that is here in this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers;	and break the second joint, and cover its joint until the moisture that is inside has gone away.
et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament;	Take the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not, then it is necessary to grease the woman with mustard plaster made from fenugreek with sesame oil.
puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre:	Then make her inhale and exhale through a cone, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour.
si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If now the child is born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc;	And if both hands are dislocated, then it is necessary to gently and slowly reset them little by little.
