Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him stitching, I doubted whether the hairs had harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and fed and watered;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they said no experts that when he has a small wound in the intestine, that he should be tied in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take thick strings, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the string has opened his mouth, then place it across both lips, so that he strains his mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cover the head, and it holds so that he cannot slip, then place the other string as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and examine the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the sharp object is in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the sharp object from the intestine of the animal that is very dirty, and then tie it to the thread of thin linen, then wrap the thread around the needle, and examine the intestine, and pull it out through the hole;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing is no further than according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the wound is large and extensive, especially when it is in one of the internal cavities, there is no remedy or health, only subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or where it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	all wounds or abscesses, when they appear, are universally called "fistulas", and specifically when they are cut and opened.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula is along the spine, a hard and white sore, where no pain is felt, and it is as sharp as the beak of an eagle.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	And sometimes clear and sometimes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	And sometimes little and sometimes enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	And I have spoken of this in the section on wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no char, it is only because of one of the EIGHT causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	It is to know, by the smallness of blood or wounds;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard clotting within, and on the lips, which does not allow blood to flow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much swelling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the joint is twisted, and the matter is of bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good for the treatment.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is like a plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and expelled by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, signs, and remedies in the chapter.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to inform you of the treatment of fistulas made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	It is said that fistulas can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the face, or to the intestines, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it comes to the property of the main member, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all these fistulas of this kind are of great suffering, and there is only labor and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is no fistula that does not come from the joint that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know the remedy, take a rain or iron tent, if the fistula is straight, if it is crooked.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is crooked, then circle it with a thin tent of wool, for the wool pours through the twists.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well encircle it with tents, then cleanse it through one of the holes, for the moisture will cut from one hole to another, and it cleans.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then correctly and carefully to your power, that you know if there is bone or nerve, and is cut in half, and ask well of the patient about the pain he feels when pressing your hand, and the limb where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you will know truly the limb where it is, and if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or any of the limbs that I have told you, then proceed according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the corrupt matter that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure until it is healthy, and if the fistula is well deeply at the right place, then you should cut in half as much as you can, then put moist bandages in medicine water, and push them into the main part of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then I apply clean, warm wax, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if it is not healed by then, cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by a fistula, cut it off.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerves do not harm your principal members, as we have said.
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean out the corruption until it is all gone, then apply clean wax until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if it is not healed, and remains bowed as before, then do not delay in seeking further treatment.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you discover and desire to be at the bottom, and remove all corruption, then restore the limb.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if it is thus healthy, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, seek that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other means than to wait for nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	And if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with pincers, if it is drawn to the appropriate tool for that, and if there are many bones, then remove them all.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	And if the moisture makes it against you, and there is no mistake or fear, then boil and moisten and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, place a warm, moistening substance on the wound to soften the bones, and leave it until the bones are surrounded by flesh, and then they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	And if they are large bones, such as a leg or thigh, then wait until the corruption is complete and the bone is completely softened, then close the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a large part of the corruption, and it comes to form a mass around the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it should be covered and covered with all around the corruption, and then treat it until it is completely healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you might take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was a young man around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, such that the matters came to the leg, and was inflamed by a large abscess, and there was no cause to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	But the wise ones over-opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they drained many matters, and it became a fistula, and there came much pain that everyone was groaning and sweating from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many sought and sought care within two years, and there was no knowledge in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw her leg and the medicines that were used to treat it, and what was running through the pores at great speed.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the veins of the young, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then I searched all the holes, and found that one was coming into contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I therefore hastened, and took from one of the pores until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption was coming into the bone from within.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I thought what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and I thought that there was no other corruption, but that which I had taken.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicines soaked in long tension, and could not stick.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	Then I re-examined, and discovered the bone as before, and found continuous corruption in the bone, and the marrow, and then I removed it, and I was unable to heal the limb.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	But I could only manage to remove as much of the bone as possible, and then treat it throughout its entire length, and then restore it with medicines.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And it healed and healed quickly, but did not want to start the work again except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was healed entirely, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction throughout, neither to the left nor to the right.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the jawbone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take a piece of cloth, and place it at the top of the bone that opens, and command that it not be extended upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and place another piece of linen, larger than the first, on top of the part that is outside the bone, and extend the jaw, so that you can remove the rotten flesh from outside, and cover the wound above the place where you want it to be, so that it does not bleed;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a bandage or a cloth outside the bone to cover the rotten flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it is necessary to be as much silk as one can see and feel the corruption, and be another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the tooth is rotten and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, then remove the whole crown.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then put the wax on one side of the corruption and then silk from one part to the other, and let the silk be as long as possible from the corruption, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupted joint and silk the bone on the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if its deformity is in the continuation of the second joints, there is no other remedy than to apply copper.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if its deformity is at the tip of the finger or toe, this is very difficult, but nevertheless you must inquire about that corrosion, how it opens.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it in all the ways you can, but do not cut the vein or the nerve against your will.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and wash those that the cutter and the threads for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of the nails, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and therefore it is necessary to arrange each similar work's tool;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the work will show you the tool that you will need to have knowledge of this art, according to the knowledge of diseases and their symptoms;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think the tool that you have according to what it should be.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder dislocates either due to moisture, or due to lack;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have cured that corrosion by the care of medicines, and it does not improve, then it is necessary to amputate that member until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the pain escapes by death, or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are such that the limb becomes black, so it seems as if it has been burned by fire, and remains black, then it goes through the corrosion of member to member, and takes hold of the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you have a bite, and if it is by the percussion of some poisonous animals, such as scorpions of the sea and snakes, and similar, if the corrosion is at the back of the neck, then the copper, and do not give it any space to come near the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes near the hand, then the copper at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come near the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it comes to the arm, then cut the copper.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the collarbone, it is death, and there is no remedy except the amount of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and then do as follows when the corrosion comes or stings:
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes to the first joint, then cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it stings, then cut all the sting.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the pain kill.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the manner of applying a bandage or a cloth to the limb is such that you tie it above and below, and extend some bandages along one side, and other bandages along the other side, and you soak the char between the two limbs at a span's width, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then the bandage or cloth, and put a piece of linen on each part, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy limb, and comes to the injury, other lesion, and abscess;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood comes out when you work, then cauterize the limb quickly, or put some astringent powders on it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to your medicine as it is accomplished, then bind the injured limb with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in the story:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	he suffered a severe burn that looked like fire, and that corrosion first affected his entire body;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the doctor saw the corrosion, he covered the body with a bandage, and it was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after some time, the corrosion returned to his hand, and it came to me, and I put him on things that were reflective after cleaning the wound, but I could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to hold his hand, and I did not want to do so unless I had hope of recovering the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the power of the ointment was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land, and stopped covering his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not counted it worth mentioning except for the purpose of doing something else if one has such business.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Abscess never comes in the joint that is greased, and it lasts for so long that it causes great swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then pierce and cut through, and into the belly, and let the limbs remain still, as if in a vat.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above is also as delicate as the cloth you remove, and does not corrode the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus", and are not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it reaches the bone in front, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And if the skin is so thin that it covers the bone all around, and even when it is as delicate as cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not become corrupted by its decay.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have sworn that the skin will not decay, and the corruption is not yet in progress, and the skin is blackened by fire, then the treatment of the ointment should be as follows:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look if the wound is large, and the belly that is in it has a putrid odor, then the ointment of Egyptian medicine made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Take garlic, oil, and litharge equally, and put them in a small vessel to boil in the fire until the medicine is red and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take as much as needed according to your necessity, and make it into a sharp and sweet mixture, and apply it to the chest, and hold the abscess open.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in place for two hours, then expel it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this as many times as necessary until the chest is clean and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never use the mixture of ash and powdered sulfur when this medicine is not present, and you should squeeze powdered vine wood, and pour boiling water over it, then let it drain, and apply it to the chest, until you know that the chest is clean.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the pain is too great for them to bear, neither Egyptian medicine nor the sharp powder of ashes, then apply a poultice of honey and clay or if they have a little bit of burnt willow bark.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you apply a poultice of honey and melted wine, where the honey has the property of healing and cleansing, and the wine makes the wound rot.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you have secured that the wound is well healed, then apply a poultice of what makes new flesh grow in it, and it is that you hold a definite plaster, and they make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	where you cauterize the wound with some medicines and ointments, of which I have described their properties or treatment of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the pain is small and the wound cannot take in the cataplasm, then enlarge it a little with a needle, and put in an Egyptian tenting or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too large, then cut and leave it open as much as possible where the cataplasm can enter, and if the pain is above the shoulder, then cover or higher up the shoulder where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	When the bow is in place, do not let the arrow stick out.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	And if you cannot cover the entire side as you see fit, then arrange it in such a way that the bow is at its lowest point where it is, for when the bow is in place, do not let the arrow stick out and if you cannot cover the entire side as you see fit, then arrange it in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bow gently slides down, and leave nothing of the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidative remedies to place on the wound, and stay on the linen cloth that covers the entire wound;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then apply the force in the right place to push back the swelling of the chest not too wide from the first, since it is stuck tightly under the other cloth according to the amount of the swelling, and put it on the wound to align the bowels, and do not remove the large drape until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is on the wound of the chest, often remove to remove the bowels, and check what comes out of the bowels, whether it is poison or little or enough, or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in a certain way and you see the nature that jumps over the wound of the chest, check if the chest is already raised, and approach the healthy side.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then dislocate it in the morning, or the next day, and when you dislocate the wound, if you change the bandage, and renew the poultice.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the chest is pushed inward after many hours, push the chest back so it does not remain misaligned.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after long tension, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who delay in applying char to their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if they apply it in an undigested manner after many days, it is possible that the breasts will not heal.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if the breasts take a long time to heal, and are distant, then apply moist medicines in substance and dry in virtue, such as poultice, because there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a definite amount of honey, and make it into a poultice with rose oil, and add an equal amount of old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use;	Then use it.
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	And this itself is made of cooked honey, when there is no raw honey present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and the powder on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	Then glue it to a cloth, and place it on the chest, and never administer it long, and roots of star anise, which is also like flour and hundred.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and in the use of simple or compound remedies:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	grind them, and make powder from them, and put on honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is long, and not cured by this cure, then scrape away the corruption that has formed, and make an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in joints;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure of the cure of the fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the elbow
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises outside the joint of the little finger of the hand, or the toe, or by chance it arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	When it is dislocated, and no precaution is taken, if it comes into contact with an abscess, and it is covered and poured with boiling water until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it covers all of it;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it comes into contact with the bone, until it reaches the point of intense pain, and the affected part is large and red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help much, then you must remove all the excess that remains from the elbow, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are very helpful if the bones are healthy, and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail is close to the flesh, and it begins to prick, and the wound, then you must put the cauterizing iron on the outside of the nail so that it does not penetrate the flesh, and bring the burnt part upwards, and carefully and gently cover this char with healing and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply poultices until they are healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then cut off and remove it, for as much as the bone has been corrupted, it cannot be healed.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the other decaying, then cut off and remove it as before mentioned, then apply poultices until they are healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	And if it is foul, swollen, and causing great pain, then you must first cleanse it.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	Then cut the infected part off with a sharp knife, making sure that the cut does not come into contact with the healthy flesh around the nail, for the pain would be too great.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if it happens, put something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The sharp pain of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The sharp pain that arises in the hands of some men by chance is all chronic, and sometimes it is in the fingers or where there are bones, and never in the nail, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or in any of the ten fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are born without any bone in the shoulder do not move, and those who are born at the joint of the shoulder may move by chance.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of the one who is chubby is lighter, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	size it at its root of a wide span.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those who are born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it with a copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In those who are born or must be at the back, it is necessary that you first cut the round bone reasonably close to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk according to this, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in two ways come from birth or from the wound, or from burning of fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is appropriate to cover that which is sore, so that it may return according to its natural forms.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Or you place between two thin pieces of wood, until the bones are sound, as they should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	When it comes to both of his hands with the palm, if that suits the healing as it should.
des vils	of the base
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large and swollen with excess melancholy, which comes from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And they come more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should never administer any purgative of clay, and then give the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The cure of iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	One is that one takes the blood and draws out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to tie the vein, and pull it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The cut is done in this way:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	First, the sharp knife is heated very hot, until the thick sinews are not thinned, then the leg is straightened from the misaligned position above the knee to the lower part of the groin;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then cut the vein in the thigh, or in the first, second, or third part, with a wide blade, then lift and pull out the black blood with your hand from one side to the other, until as many sinews as the pain can bear are removed.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and command him to rub with meat juice mixed with black pepper.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are clear, and expose to the air.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The following is done in this way:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Rub the painful leg, if there is much hair, then put it in hot water, and apply hot compresses to the leg until it turns red, and open the veins.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	If you have no hot water, heat it on the fire, and then place the heated cloth over the vein where it is long at the knee or in the lower leg.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then work the skin at the incision, and scrape the vein from every part, as it appears when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	Then push the needle through, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then you can put it lightly at the incision, then cover it in the other place with two or three fingers.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then scrape the skin over the vein as it appears, then lift it to the wound, as you have done, and put it at another incision, as you have done first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then take another size, or if you have experience with this, then lightly, and apply it to the second part of the wound, then remove it and lightly apply it to the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract the sizes in size, until all the strength is gone, then apply it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then if an arrow with a strong double point enters the thread, and tie it and remove it, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it is gone.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not stick, because if it sticks, then one cannot pull or lift it, and it causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have fully treated it, place on the wound a cloth soaked in wine and rose oil.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the care until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the wound is contracted and twisted and swollen all together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then it is necessary that you cut it painfully, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron that covers the wound is curved, and does not cut through it, so that it does not cover the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of large curvature, because if it were too fine, it would cover the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is enlarged in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land that has no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	And by chance it arises in other parts than the legs, and there is a puss that comes out from under the skin, as it comes from within the body winding and turning, enlarged between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that it comes in the leg a very large inflammation, then the limb changes, and the vein begins to issue forth, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of cloth of one and a half inches wide and two inches long, and wet it, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not there, if you wrap it around the cloth, and wet it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	If it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining part around its root, and do not cover it completely until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cover it, it will go back into the wound, and cause abscess and pus or infection in the limb, and make the patient very sick.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary that it be treated very little and very slowly from the top, and nothing should remain or rot.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there should never be this vein when it is treated with V palms of length, or X, and sometimes I have seen it come out from X palms long, and when you cover it, it will burst the skin or puncture, and go all the way down to the bottom.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and clear out the matter that is inside, and administer to the patient medicines infused for the purpose of healing any injury, then treat the wounds as you would with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never rain on this vein, and especially when it opens at the joint of the finger, or finger, and if much blood comes out, and it is difficult to stop.
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	Treat the wound as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of verses that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land, because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body, and is felt by all members to member, until it reaches the skin where it was, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the presence of certain humors, such as come from worms and lumbricus and ascarides or intestines.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and it is doubted as to its harm, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the brain, perhaps enters, and destroys the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	when you see it to cure and draw out, then one cannot do but when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then it is necessary that you hold the limb above and away from a very tightly bound bandage, then cut across and draw it out, and if it turns back into the body, then you should cauterize with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it consumes oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold the spoon firmly over it, then pour on it and remove it.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary to use the ointment of healing herbs for the diseases caused by bad humors, and if there are wounds from eating rotten meat.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "wakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	I see what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a woman with a bad arm, and I discovered that her arm was swollen, and there was a small abscess in the armpit.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And soon after, I saw it grow as large as a worm in the shoulder, much faster than anything, as if it were live silver when cut from the bone.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain departed from the arm and moved to the shoulder, then a little later it corrupted throughout the body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she twisted around her body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease move in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted to make sure that she could move the pain from one arm to the other, but I did not see her do it as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, and the veins exposed, and because that visibility was constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they do not reveal themselves to those who are delicate, and who have moist skin and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it opens as we have described, then tie above and below hastily, and then cover it so that that visibility is constrained to the limb is gone;
et cauterize le leu;	and burn the limb.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat the cause of that visibility, like foul-smelling pills, and snake pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their appearances and according to the types of bodies they penetrate.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of them is that there are those who have large points, and small ones, and pointed ones, and polished ones.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those who have II angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and that which penetrates into any member if it penetrates according to the two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a principal member such as the neck, as the spine, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it penetrates therefore into any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary for you to extract this arrow, as many die afterwards in various positions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely removed from the wound, then cut it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	and the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces and goes through the bone, and the sinus above the skull, which is blindness and swelling and sweating and redness of the throat, and spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps there is no pain in the nostrils or ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and possibly the word and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and white watery fluid like pus, and also like boiling pitch from the wound;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or enters is that it is close to the right breast, and also feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and possibly the arrow moves like pus, and also cuts through black blood, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and syncope.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then they are sent away due to doubt of death.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been pulled out is that without complaining of pus, it jumps out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limbs change color, and it gasps for breath and seeks the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the coverlet of the poor, it is behind the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and gives great pain and shortness of breath.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and move all the members of the shoulder.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the stomach, by chance if it jumps out of the wound nothing of the undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the abdomen, and it does not come out through the intestinal wall, there is no hope of cure or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead is stuck in the bladder, and the urine comes out and goes away, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Then it is clear that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and neck and throat and shoulder and back and spine and hip and knee and feet, and similar members, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who had an arrow stuck in his thigh at the root of the knee:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it, and took it out from the other side through the fat of the ear, and he was cured without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And in one game, an arrow that shot into the grease of the oil outside the paper, and the arrow was returned, and could not reach beyond the tip facing the fust, and it was a great arrow of a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The game was sound, and no harmful accidents came to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And an arrow shot into the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I healed the wounds, and skillfully treated it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And a arrow was stuck in a man, whether it was in his head or belly, and I thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty hours, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, inserted a probe, and pulled it out, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to a man who an arrow fell on or back, and the wound was sewn up from above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural conditions, and found no harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you want to another man who an arrow fell on his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and prolongs thus without great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And a spear was thrown at the man of the prince, the king, who had his head in the neck, and was slightly inclined to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the spear was entirely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I found it all in a very thin tent, and did not feel any pain.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt sharp pain and pain on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the spear. I put it on his forehead, attractive digestive, because the eyes do not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	And I placed the poultice on it immediately, and dressed the wound directly, and left it in place for a long time, until he felt the arrowhead still inside his nostril.
et il le me dist.	And he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I placed a corrosive medicine on the wound immediately, until it was open, and I tried to extract it, and felt the head of the arrow sticking in his neck.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I pushed it into the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it passed well the ends within four months, and then began to ulcerate the wound that I had sewn with needles, on one side and the other, and could not heal.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Therefore, I continued to subtly and cleverly manipulate tools, until I took the needles again, well made, according to what its form will be at the end of this chapter, so that I sew it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physician judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it anyway, and the wound was healed, and the pain was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	I have told you the quality of some arrow extractions, so that you put your care above what I do not say, for the books cannot contain everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But the wise masters compare well with little knowledge, and above what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come from members where they are stuck, unless in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the limb through which they enter, or by another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which goes through the part where it enters, is an arrow entering in its joints, and never comes out of them.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if she does not jump now, let her remain until the charcoal is burned through and the issue is alleviated.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot be removed, let her remain thus for several days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then she jumps, and if she does not jump, pierce all around with a fine needle until the flesh around is expanded, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the belly's ventricles, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if not to pull it out immediately, but let it be even for some time after, because if the arrow comes out too soon, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not firmly lodged in the bone only, and does not come out by itself, and stays for several days without causing harm, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is very stuck and cannot come out, then administer tar to it as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is reinserted into the body so that it cannot be seen, then it is hidden in the whole tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot pull it out due to the narrowness of the wound and the deepness of the arrow, and there is no bone or sinew or vein, then leave it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and if you find the arrow, and if it has ears in the arrow that it holds, then break the char that is stuck to two parts of the muscle that you can, and then break or pull out the ears of the arrow, as much as you can pull it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully do not break the shaft, so that you can pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it once, then push the lung back inside through the ribs, as extraction causes pain.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding of blood makes you contrary, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put effort as you can muscle to pull out the arrow without danger, or soon or late, or tightly or firmly;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Put the patient according to the shape it was in when the arrow hit, for this is the greatest help, and if you cannot, put it according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another part, where it opens nothing, or the skin is swollen in that place where one can see or feel it.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then cut above, as far as the hooks can take, and then extract it.
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, round your hand and push it into the bone until it enters, then expand the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it in and then restart the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it is from an arrow and it is, if it is stuck in the whole body;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is stuck in the chest, and you see that it is administered slowly, if it is administered with a tool, so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the tool;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then pull out, and if the arrow is stuck, if it is pulled out with the tool entering pointedly, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all of the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is stuck in the back or belly or in the stomach or bladder or side, and it is close, and you can cover it up, if it can be covered.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and do not cover the vein and the limb, then pull it out, and then suture the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and continue the treatment until they are healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the amount of blood.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is like the beak of a bird, to stick into the point of the arrow, such as this shape.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the barbs to stick and to hold is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins that can be tapped from which one has or takes 16, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	2 bananas that are after the ears, which are called the two "herbaceous";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the two temples apparent;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are called "aspirants";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is behind the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the neck;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augicherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cervical, and is on the right side of the chest, and is called the "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	The moxa is called "hast", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilar, and they call it the lay people "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilar is on the right side, and they call it the lay people "vein of the belly", and it is above the sacrum, and it is that from which one heals, which opens obviously above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the savatte is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it has rain.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the leg and where the knee is, there are three veins:
