l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is outside the pouch of the left rib cage, and the second is above the knee on the right side.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the knee of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three veins besides those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The cleansing of the veins that are after the ears helps with ancient catarrh and headaches.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the quality of the cleaner, as I told you, and that you rub the head of the pain, and rub the limb where the veins are on a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then press the painful spots on their neck to a noose, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two folds of the neck.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	For the questions you have about your shoulder, and where you feel the hairs away from your shoulder, if they are painful, squeeze them.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the needle, and the thread from outside the vein to the bone, then lift your hand above the vein, and cut and remove the skin and the vein well, you must pass through it twice, and let out the pus until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then drain and bandage, as long as it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is better to embrace them gently, and soothe them, and apply a custom-made compress to them.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of a good surgeon are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and that he holds his head steady, so that both veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the hairs on his chin, and then shaves them;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the skin over the vein at the chin index, and prick it with a lancet outside, and lift the vein upwards, and cover it as you have done in the other veins, and draw off the blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the dislocation, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a bandage, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of them and their treatment and extraction, which begins the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the facial veins is as valuable as the healing of headaches and ancient facial diseases, and migraines, and rheumatism.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality of the pain is such that the patient twists their neck, until the vein appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool called "fossil", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip of it on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then relieve the pain by loosening the neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and only once in a while with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, the fire should not be too hot.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	And the cauterizing iron should be straight, because the teeth are close, and by chance it may break the flame when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cauterizing of the two veins that are in the two arms helps them, and at the elbow, and at the wrist, and at the eye in the oil, and for diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their cauterizing is such that the pain is relieved by twisting any ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and let the health pass through the wound, a little long of the flame, a little wide, for there is no hair.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the fire is too fine, perhaps it will break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then apply cotton to the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie it up and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein in the neck is useful against ague, and for sudden swelling, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and constantly when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the health is such that the pain is strained at the neck, then strain the neck to your right hand, and take the fine fire long, and put it between the lip and the space between the two noses, for the vein does not open well on its own, and the saint will begin to bleed now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not move it too much, and apply the bloodletting according to your need, then bind it for a night, as it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The oil of the two myrtles helps to narrow the almond, and at the beginning of melting, and for many diseases, and for impetigo, and for corrosions, and for herpes, and for stomatitis.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the oil is such that the pains stray from both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And let the masters be above the top of the pain, and the pain lies across one seat, then oil the long one a little widely, then apply the bloodletting gradually, as much as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then perform the other vein, then release the artery, and hold the veins steady, so they do not constrict.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it bleed until morning, so the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the liver above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and mouth sores and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bandage is to place the wound in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right cheek and the other on the left, which are black, and by which there are small black veins inside.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Therefore, examine both sides, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, compare the largest of each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the tongue's disorder
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The veins that are below the tongue help after the venipuncture of the cephalic, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the venipuncturist is that the diseases cease between your hands before the sun, and you lift the tongue, and look away on each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore, both are healthy and do not move too quickly, for they are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins that are commonly treated are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by pricking at all the fire with a wide needle, or with an oil lamp as thin as a thread, and is called "anevil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and thickness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirror is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And there is skill for opening the veins that are coarse and flat, which contain large clots and disturbed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the thin needle fire:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtlely pointed, and is for purifying veins that are subtle, where there is subtle blood yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purgation of the basilicon, which is one of those veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the shoulder, and where the arm, and where the stomach.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the purger to do so skillfully, and to avoid the artery that is outside.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he pierces the artery, and blood flows out, then it is necessary to apply a compress as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And he should not hold the fire, but cut as with scissors.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilicon does not open clearly, then it is necessary to strain and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	where you want any pain from it, or you know how to put it back in place instead of the vein in the arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the copper to the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the limb of the injury, then it is necessary that you strain the arm, so that you touch the limb as much as you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then sign the wound with ink, and then tie the arm, and put the vein in the fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the limb swell, for it is the artery:
eschui la donques.	eschar the wound then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding as high as the urine of a child, and the discharge is red and thin, know that it is from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then quickly apply your finger over a long distance, then remove your finger over the discharge, which often occurs;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the hairs;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be in fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the discharge is not stopped, and it hurts, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery open, for the head of the arrow may be drawn back;
et estainche li sans.	and stains the skin.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of bread, and tear it, and take one half and soak it well in the other juice;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if the skin is not stained, it is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, as we have said, treat with powders that stain blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stains are not too dark in many positions for the small limb of the wound, and the position of the patient's arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The cleansing of the vein in the middle helps that it treats blood above and below, because it is composed of basilica and cephalic, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it is necessary for the doctor to stretch out for the limb that is dislocated, and if he does not do it too forcefully, and he finds the limb, and he inflates it and the wound is not healed;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this limb is often open many times, and if it does not open in any men due to its subtlety, then you must use the instruments of the doctor;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and protect the limb from your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The doctor of the head helps, that she draws blood from the head, and helps to those;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary for the doctor to prick with the oil lamp or the mint lamp, because it is the safest of all veins, because it has no joints or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	In all cases, one should seek the lightest limb, and not cause any harm if it is necessary for the first time, and then restart.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, some men's limbs may swell up, but it does not cause any harm the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about healing is that healing is not intended for any other purpose than to maintain health and prevent diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And the healing should be done in one of the three veins that are open:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, cephalic, median, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should begin to fasten in the beginning of the first ten days, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one should begin to fasten the first day or the third, after two hours or three in the morning.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The fastening that is administered for diseases has no determined time, but rather it depends on the hour or the food, in every hour and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And one should not fasten children under the age of twelve, nor a woman who is pregnant except for low abdominal pain up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nor should one heal the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to purify themselves in any way that they may, it is necessary for them to cleanse their intestines from a light clyster, if they have much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract the excess and superfluous intestinal matter that harms the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor does one purify those who are too clean of meats, or those who are bloated, as much as they may be, nor hydrotherapeutic.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one wishes to purify after colic passion, vomiting, and diarrhea, and frequently changing of habits, of traveling, of watching and fasting, and all the virtue, or by some means of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then carefully remove the humors, if it is not too large, through food and drinks and through medicines, if you have the ability.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter or bathe, if nothing prevents it, to thin the blood and cleanse the veins from the worst in the third, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and avoid that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be tied and joyful, and let the healer be higher than that one who is being healed, and rub the arm twice or three times, then restrict the movement of the joint above, for when it is too loose or tight, it cannot be corrected.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the limb with hands, until the veins swell, and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the vein with a drop of old oil, then place his finger on the hand nearest to the vein where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not burst and fail to draw blood.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that burst as if they were strings to the bleeding, and some are so thin in flexibility, that when one puts on the fire, they withdraw from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if he opens the vein, if the wound is too narrow, because it is necessary that the bleeder be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if you see this work for the first time, it is good.
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, then restart a little below or above, if the part is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the part is inflamed, and the pains subside, then leave it for a day or two, and do not bind the arm tightly.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	Perchance I will bring abscesses afterwards.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Do not enter or take a bath, then restart the cleansing if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the pain is small, or if you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you have seen, then apply heat directly to the wound.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and the work is done rather harshly, as long as the patient's breath is not held;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swelling, do not start again with the wound cleaning, and put a little bit of oil on it, because it soothes the pain of the stone, and is more effective in this limb than the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil remedy in each cleaning to stop the flow of the stone.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this itself causes a tracheotomy and suffocation when put on the limb.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly, separate the teeth when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there are large abscesses that often occur, specifically when it is not cleaned except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and place an absorbent sponge soaked in boiled and strained vinegar on the limb for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary to do this after the discharge of the blood from the vein, and if it remains on the limb for any days without any blackness or greenish color, then it does not need to be removed.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place anything of aloes or of mustard mixed with juice of camomile, monsterwort, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often appears to be an abscess at the base of the church:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	So put your hand on it, and if you feel the bone moving under the pressure of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore do not put anything on it that we have said, because accidentally you might cut the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but rather apply a dry bandage to harden the bone, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And follow each vein according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is not black, let it bleed as long as it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see that it is thick, let it bleed as long as it becomes thinned out;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is appropriate for the one who is skilled and experienced, and has the task of extracting arrows, to make a larger wound, and to use wide flames;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is appropriate to bandage often and little, and it should be bandaged by cutting across, not by pinching;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bandaging is safe from the corrosion of arrows and the compression of nerves, and it is better than long or wide bandaging.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one whose body needs bandaging, it is appropriate to give bread soaked in juice of green grapes;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is hot-tempered, take three or four bloodlettings with warm blood; and if it is of cold complexion, change the bread before the saint's day into a moistened, sweetened bread in a musky syrup, or an aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and coriander, and a strongly scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he palms the wound after much bleeding of blood, it is necessary that he drink broth of char, and sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to strengthen an arm, and wound again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bandage gradually and gradually, according to the amount of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to wound again an arm after the first bleeding, and he has great pain, he should bandage seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the second hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal on the other side, they should heal according to the second hour or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For it has much blood within the body that is already hot, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bursts;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must restore all the conditions of health, and place your hand on the pulse when it is healed, so that many die in place of the vein, and this often happens when the healer is neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not matter whether you see the shoulder sliding out of its place, and making a cut again, and the wound is closed, that you press firmly on;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	and if it is crooked, extend the arm quickly, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it rest until it heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you have not at the tip of the flame, until the uncongealed blood flows from the wound, and put on a small piece of cloth to stop the bleeding, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if it flees, let it go and do not hold it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary, draw the blood from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is safer than the main one because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of healing is that the hairs put their hand in hot water until the wound is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it gently, so that the vein appears well, then clean it thoroughly, neither too narrow nor too wide;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let it bleed widely, and clean it well near the joint of the hand, and if none can come out, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is already in that state, do not put the hand in hot water again, for it will freeze more than it is already;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the cleaning of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The right hand's savior from all diseases of the liver is as follows:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strain the hand, and boil in very hot water until the vein is broken, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the savior is crooked, and if you hold it with both hands, it will not hurt anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Do not remove it too soon from the fire, for the nerves are all stripped of flesh, and then put the hand back in very hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and it cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary, put oil and silk on the vein to sew quickly, and thus do for each part.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The right side of the hand is useful for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The left side of the hand is useful for all diseases that are outside the body, such as diseases of the marsh, retention of urine, and diseases of the feet, knees, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its savior is such that the pains boil well in very hot water, and rub on the vein until it rots, and tie above the joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the elbow, and from above the flesh goes out much of rain.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then give the larger or more water, or at the elbow, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you give it above the flesh, then beware of the nerves which are dislocated, and give it across as in bandaging.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the bone, reset the joint in high places, and let the vein well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the first giving is not enough, then start the second above a little, because the veins are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	and do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and thus give the other bandage equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the neck is at the elbow, and its resetting is equal to the pain of the back, when it comes to arrow removal.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in the baths, and strangulate above the ankle four times in twisting, for otherwise it does not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then the healthy one in all ways that you can, and in crossing;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worthwhile to cover it, for the veins are dry, and it is very difficult to find.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not cover it, then the vein of the one who opens or falls asleep at the little finger, and towards the little toe, and guards against the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and make so much correction of the blood that you see, and then remove the sinew, and place it on cotton and hold it tight;
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuums are made of horns, or of brass, or of glass;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And suction is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this suction without pricking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is at full heat, or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And suction done by pricking and drawing blood is done in twelve steps of the body, of which one is at the top of the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in the second rib of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction from the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction on both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the buttocks.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suctions in both arms.
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suctions in both legs.
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suctions in both knees.
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the body, and because of this, it does not weaken anyone, as one does with the treatment of bloodletting.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should only be administered, not at all times or in all fevers, in no disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessary for diseases, it is recommended to ventose, or for customs, if you amnistron each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every ten days.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have business to ventose, have heavy heads;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if some have repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and at the neck, and tormented by them;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and reach for blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who dream, and see through blood and nausea and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we order them to fast after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The sweating of the muscle helps to ease the pain of the shoulder ... that comes from the eyes, and it should not be done except after the evacuation of all the blood.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in place of the sweating of the head, and it should not be done except for those of cold complexion or who have diarrhea, because this does great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore it should not be done for those who are awake or have severe cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often have this, become forgetful, and for that reason, it is necessary to place the vacuum a little more below due to the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the sweating of the shoulder and the basilica, and because it is good for the narrowing of the windpipe, and for the lengthening of the throat, and for all, and for repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is best to place it not too tightly, for if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction or stomach and intestine pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the second costal cartilage of the chest is beneficial for head pain, obtunded and emaciated, and choking, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is in the place of the health of the basilica;
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is best that you command the healthy person to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not compress the artery, and does not cause blood to spurt.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation of the lower jaw is beneficial for mouth disease, and decay of teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and is in the joint of the lower lip.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilations of the shoulders are useful for diseases that come from heat and overfilling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The winds of the neck are as valuable as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the patient not to fear too much in the presence of blood, for the veins are bare of flesh, and can be seen and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction cup that is above the back is as valuable as emergency surgery at the foundation, and for diseases that cannot be seen, and it should be large and made of metal, so it can effectively draw out.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And perhaps, if it is too fine, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	et il faut grand soin.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles attirent du sang de tout le corps, et valent aux douleurs anciennes des reins, et de la marie, et de la vessie, et ramiennent les fluides;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	et sont en l'emplacement des deux sophénes, et des deux chevilles, et toute la vie elles affaiblissent le corps après longs usages, et font venir paumonie dans plusieurs conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	Le manière de mettre la ventouse est ainsi que tu la mettes premier vide, et succe temprement, et la met fermement, et remue igalement, et ne cesse de ce faire, tant que tu voies le lieu rouge et enflé, et apparait le rougeur du sang;
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	then firmly, and reset the suction cups, and take care in the positioning of the limbs, for there are some who have tender skin and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to strike once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds and one deep one;
et suce legierement.	and clean lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the wound is not large, then it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	the first time to puncture the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the wound is not very deep, then it is necessary to strike the third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out a little blood at a time, then we should suck only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish to draw much blood, we recommend frequently.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is not drawn, we advise using a sharp, pointed instrument, and the ends should be well perceived, suitable for those who have thick skin and are tough, and who have hard pores, that you oil the mouthpieces of the vacuum with an appetizing and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of purple oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the other state, of lettuce oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of tamarisk, or balm, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person who is to be treated with a hot bath and wide pores, then one should not put any oil, but it should be washed after the vaporization of high rose water, or high cold water, or marjoram water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or high mint water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive fullness should rise from old wine, or vinegar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and should not be immediately saunier of suction before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and should not sleep immediately after suction, and it is good that they warm up, when they should be sucked and when they are being sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And if those who are sucked are choleric, and if they do not have enough, they become too agitated and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is good that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and leeks at the spoon, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And put on wet bandages, and charcoal from Chastelron, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine of medium age, which is between old and new, and put on a little, and wet bandages and moist meats and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day he starts walking, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is recommended to give some men once truffle or muscat wine before walking, or after, to strengthen the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And it should be made subtle for the sick, but only those who are strong should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are applied to cause pain are those that are applied to the liver, and to the mouse, and to the gout, and to the belly and the buttocks and the rain and the waist, for these members do not suffer pain from other places, and no one does so except to draw blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the newborn cries;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the buttocks to soften the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain, when there is an abscess or stone, by its attractive virtue perhaps the abscess, or to remove the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	Then it is done like this when putting it above the liver and above the stomach when there is wind retention, and these vacuums are administered empty for suction only.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And never are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain hot tea, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a way that the vacuum is filled with hot steam, or hot water in which he has cooked poisonous herbs to this lung.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half-palm-sized openings and a cost of the middle I small perforation, as to put a needle, and if it is of silver, so that it does not bleach the wound when putting it above the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and have a long, thin rod of iron or wood, to put a probe in place, and it should be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups of children are different from the old, and thin ones are different from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the probe of wax or liniment, and put it into the suction cup at the end of the rod that is in the suction cup, so that it clears the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the hair.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	then place it above the member, and you should be above the opening that we have said, so that when you want to, then the steam goes in, and open the vacuum.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and grasp the line as before, and repeat often if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the vacuum that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all sharp, does not have a rod or an opening, and is not administered until it is full of sharp, and is placed above the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Noses are not administered until in members where one cannot place vacuums for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and when removing a horse's shoe, as with one or two nails, and other similar things;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you try to remove nails that are in soft water without any difficulty, if you can;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in soft water until they are familiar and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then clean the vein and the wound, then rub the limb until it is red, and put the nails on top;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and blackened, and if it is possible to put a vacuum where, then put it, for this is very good afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the limb from below, and then from above, very well, and then wipe it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb is too clean after the wound of the sweat, then wet the linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the wound is cleaned.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds multiply, then put on broken glass, or salt, and similar things, until it is cleaned.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of the crushed beans on the limb, and let them stay until they stick to the limb, then it will stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more difficult ones, take other remedies.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the remedies do not take effect, rub the affected area with fresh blood from a vein, or make a small incision where the arrow is inserted, and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will burn;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they have fallen off, powder them with a little bit of aloe and crushed garlic, or ashes, they will now burn.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Pay attention, young apprentice, that the foolish ones who read this chapter do not see any of the old books, nor have they ever read them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, knowledge is lacking in our land, for I have never found any good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except by the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have written about it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are necessary, as I have done in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise put his understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced seek and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain comes to any one, it is necessary for you to hasten to treat the pain on both sides, if nothing stops you, as in weakness of body, or children, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If the limb is not very warm or too cold.
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	And use warm lard, that is to say, warm oils, and egg yolk and goose fat, and do not drink wine, nor use any thick broths, and do not eat too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess or spread of matter in the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the hairs return to their previous government as they used to be.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a thick mash of meat that causes swelling, such as cooked wheat, and risotto, and tests, and fish, and chicken, and eggs, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the mash should be applied frequently and soon after the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old people and the elderly cannot be properly healed or sutured according to their nature due to the corruption of the limbs, nor the same as those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not treat, reset over the broken bone and large thick rods that support and join the limb together, until it is strong as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and not at all in its work, and for this reason it must be nourished with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes through the spine, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way it should have its own willpower, and its proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory comes in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known the breakage of the bone because the leg is twisted, and open well by default, and its pressure against the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting and it is not against the touch, and the pains are not much, if there is no breakage.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can also have twisting, or cutting, or small breaking.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it by hand, but place the remedies that come here after, and then gently restrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	and the break that goes into the spiral, and the two parts are dislocated, now you must put them back evenly, as if abscesses come alive;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come alive, do not let any pus, until the abscesses are calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it back evenly to the muscle that you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of this one where there are pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold it as it should be afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	If the bone is broken into pieces, if it is two parts, if it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken bone are joined, it is reset by all means in their proper places so that you may not cause further injury or pain;
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and well support the two bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it with your hand if it seems not quite right:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the dislocation is severe, and it is not pulled back too much, and not pressed as those who bring it by their work cause abscess and contraction in the limb, as we have experienced many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, properly treat the pain so it does not move, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the limb is secure so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not in place, and it should be put in the correct position so that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and ensure it is placed correctly, as twisting should not occur when it is returned.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The quality of the limb broken is different in size and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is appropriate to wrap them with soft and thin linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is appropriate to wrap with a wide and sturdy cloth, because the large limbs embrace the entire large member, and hold it evenly in all parts, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then lightly tie it around the leg, three or four turns depending on the member, and hold your hand a little on the entire limb, then go above the fracture and hold it less than the fracture, then slowly move away from the fracture.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually soften the limb little by little, until you press a large part of the healthy leg, then take another limb and turn back around the broken leg.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part away from the fracture and hold it gently, neither too hard nor too forcefully, as we have said in the first section above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the limbs wet linen or cloths, as long as they are even, then tie everything together with a bandage, and then put your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something soothing on top of the abscess, and what removes the swelling, and leave it like this for some time.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain over your splints, and they should be half of a wide bandage cut neatly, or of rope that is made into ropes, or of reeds, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the screw that one puts over the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is needed for the limb of small or great size;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then screwed on the screws as you did in the first step, then tied with a thread evenly, as in the first step above the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is, the less;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it should be that the thread is medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen works of fools who make their bindings too thick with linen cords, and that is great error, because the bandage cannot be even if it is too fine, and should only have between each screw less than a quarter of an inch space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the thorns after the straining in their place, put discharge from them with linen, or other clean cloth, so that it does not fester.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splinter, and the stitches are broken, I will tell you the treatment here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, one should not put splints immediately after 5 days or 7, or more depending on the safety of abscess healing;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and see the manner of ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take some flour that is held in the walls of the mill, and knead it with abundant water, and put this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fracture to various positions, and especially to women and small children, for it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of applying plaster to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take alabaster, daniel, enule, asafetida, Arabic gum, and mugwort, of each equal parts;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, of each five drachms;
alechil VIIII З.;	eight ounces of oil.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make a powder, and mix it with honey.
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of applying plaster that is good for twists:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take a sharp knife and cut along the vein, at point X.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Apply a bandage and ointment, at point VIIII.
acaice VI З.;	Apply pressure at point VI.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Grind up belladonna root at point X, mix it with either vinegar or plenty of oil, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat joints and bones that are damaged is to apply a poultice, ease the pain, and use a bandage to support the bone and the broken part.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take new linen, dip it in oil and vinegar, and place it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal immediately, but it is good for relieving abscesses and properly treating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of splinting to restore broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig branches and earth pavement, grind them together, and make a splint.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method to treat the break in the bone and to ease the remaining pain of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take valerian root, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of each one in equal parts;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	grind and mix with wine, and if the limbs are hot, apply the mixture with fresh or dry coriander juice, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of treatment, more suitable than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
