Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take valerian root, linseed, balm, melilot, and without wine, and violet and chamomile flowers, of all one equal part;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And bruise, and cook with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb except for a plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to heal, dry things slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take fly and horsehair from the eye, or feathers of an owl, and vitriol, and silk equally, and grind them, and make a plaster and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove it after a while, and be careful that the hairs do not cause any pain, nor move the bones of its limb.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if not remove by hand later.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, with rest or inflammation, then hurry and reset it, and remove the plaster now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And take light bandages, and wet seaweed, and soak in vinegar, and lift the limb, until the itching stops, and let the pain be relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then apply dry linen, soak in vinegar or rose oil, and tie with a bandage, until you are sure of no abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	And relieve the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain be removed, then begin the thin bandage and a little plaster, and do not strain it as much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and subtly until they are clean.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed, and you have knowledge of plasters and ointments, then apply them evenly as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb as we have said within three days or four or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leaves it for twenty days, as we see, until the fractured bone is set and approaches the position of the chariot above;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	therefore the splint is applied again, and it increases its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb drier than usual, then no humor can come;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then rub the affected area with hot water every time you dislocate it, and this should be done daily, and release the ligament a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this work, therefore, cut the broken bones of the limb, and quickly realign it as they do with the foolish, who twist the limb painfully:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is evil, and this work is not sure, and I see nothing but pain and the correct way of working.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	many ways of breaking are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinct:
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because it has breaks that are made by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone fractures the entire bone just below the bone, as if crushed or broken;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this type of break is called «crushing».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	When the spearhead strikes the bone from above, piercing through, and is called this type of fracture "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and is the wound of these two fractures, great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from a fall, or a cut from a sword, or a break from a fall on stone, or from falling onto something else, and similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a broken bone that pierces through the skin, approaching the flesh on either side of the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is set in the bone as subtly as hair, and is the fracture small, and because of this it is called this type of fracture "hairline";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound that is made by being pierced with an arrow, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and is the threads as when they make the stove when they strike above the stoves.
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And it has more in those who have or main moist bones, as of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and it has all these ways of breaking that small pieces are discharged as these;
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of fractures by the displacement above them, and the inspection of tents, and by the rotten char that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair is known because when one has revealed the bone, and one rubs it above, if there is an open black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, be careful about the bad accident, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and turning red, and other similar things in many dispositions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any apparent injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the leg, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day or you will not be able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the arm, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the flesh around the bone has not decayed, and the injury that we have mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the linen that covers the brain, then it is necessary that you cut the broken part as follows:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and is that you press the head of the painful part, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and when blood comes to discover the bone, or abscess chaus, if it helps what it is necessary, and is that you fill the place with moistened cloths in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And let the wound rest until the abscesses have subsided, and ensure that there is no bleeding.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin around the bone to cut, and this is done according to two methods of surgery:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is that you cut narrowly in front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then use another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have many different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they are sharp and made of iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And work carefully, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and protruding, it is necessary that you drill around it, so that you administer cuts with targes, not until it goes beyond the bone of the test, and should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not let the point go beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you must have many, so that each comes in its own time of the bone's growth, so that you have splints for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three methods of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	the quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one splint on top of the bone and turn your hands so that you feel that the bone has been pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then replace the splint on another part slightly afterward, and thus do all around, then cover the incisions of the space of the bone between the pieces, and do it as subtly as you can, lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and beware of not touching the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is advisable to close the opening that has remained from the bone with all other tools similar to an incisor, but it is necessary that it be thinner and more subtle than the other incisor;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if nothing remains of the small bones or scales, do not remove them gently with all the tools;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then treat the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is this one that the Greeks say, which is more safe;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the pain is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have removed that part, then place the lens-shaped piece of this incision, which is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut into one part, and it is the affected part in the second ribs, so that the cutter is towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike with a small hammer above, so that you can slightly cut around the bone, and be careful of the wire that is outside.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is attached to the bone, then slightly cut around it, for one can cut well without hurting or fearing.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken on one side, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with a thin razor that you should have in various quantities, to manage each limb as conveniently as possible, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have large razors before, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair shears and delicate cuts, it is necessary that you anesthetize according to its advancement.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	This is a thing that cannot be answered by one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer from above another cloth, and do not strain it until it stains the wound only.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it remain there for one or two days until the abscess is soothed, then release it, and administer medicines such as lis roots, flour of vetches, powder of incense, aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and make a powder from these things, and put it on the wound, and administer mediocre medicines without causing pain;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and make sure that the wound is kept clean, that you do not leave any pus in it, or any blood clot, because when a blood clot forms on the surface of the brain, it will cause damage and harm;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when one puts a sharp object on top of the wound, it does not bite from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take precautions therefore, as no accidents come to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other means come except by the medicine that was put on top, which has virtue, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of red oil and one piece of cloth, and put it on top of the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the wound with the appropriate methods until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	It is said that never are both parts of the nose above broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that one is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it is dislocated or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small nail or needle through the breakage into your index finger, and place it evenly within the breakage at the pouch by default, until the nail regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this lightly, and ensure that the hairs do not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot reach your finger, it is necessary that you place it at the top of a small stick or a slightly thick one.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the breakage is of two parts, then repair the other part, and hurry to restore the first joint if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the abscesses have calmed down, then poke at the tip of the nail with a piece of linen cloth, if the breakage is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Where you go to one side or the other, if the break is there.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and if the tents are so large that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said no one should mash the tents in the fire, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is right, but it is necessary that they be ground in the making of an ointment from honey and powdered mille.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent until the bone is iron and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never use feathers in place of tents, and if there is a soft cloth around the wound, and if the breaker holds it, and blows the pain away.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you work, put clay or a cotton ball soaked in red wine or a little hydrogen peroxide on it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there are no abscesses, apply a poultice made of flour of mustard and powder of incense, confectioned with an egg, then place it on light bandages, and do not bind the wound tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bone is broken into small pieces, and it is broken into smaller pieces, then remove them with suitable instruments, then cut away the fracture, and treat the injury with suitable remedies and bandages, as with plasters and ointments suitable for the wound.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound in the nose, then treat with tents, and put in plugs until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is only slight, and not completely broken into two pieces, as can be seen if one looks carefully.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you bite your own index finger in the patient's mouth.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the fracture is on the left mandible, bite your own index finger with your right hand, and gently apply pressure to the fracture, and hold it steady with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is in two pieces, it is necessary that you administer traction of two parts, until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or loosening, then strain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place the fractured jaw on the broken jaw, and place it under a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	Put a large, well-made cloth or a piece of evenly cut leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, on top of the blanket, and tie it securely with a rope that you have, and command the patient to rest, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the position changes, then reset it to the tiger's shoulder, and then put it back as it was changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And put a poultice on top, with flour from the mill mixed with plenty of urine or semolina, after you have removed the crust.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And put a lighter poultice on top of that, and if the poultice sticks to the patient, and the position of the patient does not change, leave him until he is healthy.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a break and wound together, do not touch any part of the bone that is fractured.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If too subtly from the fracture with instruments to the mouth.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, if the wound is wide, then apply wound dressings to it, to drain pus until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forearm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forceful break several times before, behind the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and separated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the most light to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is that if the fracture is with wound, that you have two assistants, so that one treats the help that feels the forceful broken.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make even the fracture at your fingers, so that it forms as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have the skill to extend further, put a round, cloth or linen ball under the shoulder, according to your needs;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and extend and relieve the tendon, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you make even the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the shoulder of the arm out, because it comes from above, then it is necessary that the hairs be pulled evenly over its surface, and move the shoulder outwards, and bend the minister's elbow down, until the bone of the arm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then bring the fracture to your fingers, and if you find the pieces scattered, it is necessary that you cut across;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and try to find the lighter pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined due to any obstacle, then use one of the incisors that you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but put the forceps of this instrument out of the way to avoid the sinus:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it seems like a spoon, and is not too tight, and should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the workman;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and it should have two prongs, as you see, and one wide and the other narrow, like the edge of the wound that you made when you cut the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of an abscess, if the wound is bleeding, and if the tear is small, or you doubt an abscess, apply the wound with bandages and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it is soft, then soak the cloth in rose oil and in vinegar and in wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stripping of the bone, when it is sensitive to pain and cutting, is that you place on the bone the plaster from the mill and some flour, and put light dressings on, and put a sphere outside the wound, if you have the skill.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very wide bandage of a palm's width, then put the bandage doubled over the dressing and plaster.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a thin stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the dislocated joint, so that the head of the dislocated joint is suspended;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the stake on the broken part, and turn the joint back into its place, and dislocate the healthy shoulder, and dislocate the injured shoulder;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the injured part holds the broken part evenly, and you clearly see that the stake does not move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the joint is released, then hold it;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and place the injured limb on its back, and put a small pad under the shoulder to raise the dislocation upwards;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if the fracture of the humerus is aligned by aligning the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and it does not dislocate if no bad accidents occur within 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then restart the bandage if you see that there is a need for it, and hold it and let it be thus until it is restored;
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored within 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Few have had their shoulder broken or the arm torn from its joint, except by violent means;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the fracture follows the shape of the break, and it is reset according to its natural form, in all possible ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the arm powder from the mill with plenty of honey, and light bandages, and place above the sling double;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then place above a wide and thin board, somewhat larger than the shoulder, and do not let the board touch any part of the shoulder, so that the board is evenly supported by the bandages made of linen;
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	Then tightly bind it with a thick bandage so that the joint does not move from its place, and examine the injury every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And whenever it is displaced, tightly bind it and put the joint back in its place if it is out of alignment, and reduce the pain on its side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, reset it and be careful, for it is not bones that move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is torn off before the wound is opened, and not removed from the surrounding area, then cut through it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the splint to alleviate an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the splint
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The foot is never broken in the middle, but this rarely happens.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks again.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines towards the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of movement, and everything, and possibly vomits blood, and the wound opens in the broken bone, and the smell is bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the dislocated joint is often pushed back up onto its place, and the arm is placed between the shoulder blades, then press the shoulders, and bring together the ribs of both sides to your hands, and subtly put it in place in all ways that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put plasters and suppositories above the bone of salt, or another light one, and wrap it in a bandage, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and turn the bandage around the back, and tightly bind it, and reward every hour, and if it dislocates again, then bind it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	If it is necessary to slip it off due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, if you hasten, and slip it off, and scrape the dressing, and address what has come from methods of treatment;
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the bandage, and hold it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Note that the rib breaker only comes in the large gross after the back, and at the top, and does not press unless because they are sharp;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the smell is good at the inspection as it should be.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedies are that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and the bandage of a splint if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the rib fracture is leaning inwards, it causes great pain and sharpness, as if from weeping, for the bone does not touch the skin.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and there is much swelling and blood, and it is a great sickness, and the ancients put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, to push the broken bone into place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, if pus does not come, unless it comes.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said none of those who put suction cups on the limb, to draw out well, and it seems reasonable;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	nevertheless, doubt and because the suction does not draw out the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that among those who must cover the limb with linen oiled high, and one puts tents between the ribs to keep the lung evenly inside, then treat the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the pain is so great that it cannot be borne by the bone that does not touch the skin, and there is doubt, then it is necessary to cut across the rib on the side of the fracture, and it is necessary to place a probe to ward off the pus.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must drill the bone, and gently pull it, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments, until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if pus comes out, put moistened cloths on it in red oil, and put on the limb;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat it as needed for the abscess, and lie down near it on the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck bone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	Never come breakers to broken bones of the neck, and only a little blood comes out;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is fatal in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and do not, it means that the bone joint is saved, and the pain has been cured, if you put care on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, take note whether the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands are present, and above the back there is ventosities and involuntary egestion;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is laid on its stomach, there is involuntary egestion.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is placed on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It is deadly.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if you do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, it is the lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the care is that you reward if there is an abscess clean, put on the spine rose oil or chicken grease, until it is calmed;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then place one of the comforting and drying plasters on top, and tie it with a bandage, and command the pain to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep over that part where he feels the pain, until it is completely healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dry, it should be covered with oil.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And break the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, to one stitch, then apply the healing ointment with charcoal, until it is completely healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the fractured bone is called the "crossbone," take your right hand's fist and place it on the other hand to your power, then place the plaster and the splint on top, if you have skill.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then restrain it, and if there is bone deviation, do the same, and the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if it does, there is no great harm in a slight reduction at the neck;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	and then extend it long, and incline to the shoulder, and come to the painful limb, and swelling, and that which is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as high as you are above the breaker;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and squeeze those which are broken and the shape of the bone;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	If the fracture is only at the head, then set that fracture until it is in its natural position.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or it inclines towards the inside, place the injured limb on its belly until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it, then apply the plaster, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fractured part so it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And place the limb alongside the ribs, until the ribs are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to lie on their uninjured side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess comes, do not touch it until it is calmed down, and then follow what we have previously said.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	Then return to the resetting, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is how
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The auxiliaries are the part between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is that you take a piece of gristle of equal size, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and tie the two ends together, and raise them up, and cut off the pain above the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the broken arm through the sleeve, until it reaches its ease, and has in its middle a peg of wood, then raise it above any heavy thing or the nurse extends below;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the broken bone fragments together with both hands until the broken bone returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to place the dislocation above its shoulder, and hold the hand on its collar, then command two ministers that one ties what is above the breaker at his hands, and the other ties behind everything, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the rope outside the breaker, above the breaker, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the broken bone is near the shoulder joint, then it is necessary to place the middle of the arm away from the shoulder, and the other towards the ribs, away from the broken bone.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And if the broken bone is towards the ribs, then it is necessary to place the middle of the arm gently, with slight pressure, until the broken bone is even with the shoulder and the ribs.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then place the broken bone evenly as it should be, and hold it in place if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses come, do not restrain it for seven days, and place on it a poultice of linseed and rose oil, until the abscess is soothed;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then restrain it, and the way to restrain it is that you place the bandage on the fractured part, then bring the arm over the dislocated joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and place the bandage, and restrain over the dislocated joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bones are not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, and have two spaces between each splint, and each splint should be so large that it passes the fracture three inches from each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain against the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less with each distance.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the splints and the strain, as we have said in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is not healed, leave it to lie for seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then examine every three days the joint, that the pricking does not come to the bone, or the inflammation cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the dislocation, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents come, then wait until after three days or more, and let the pain lie on its back, and have its hands on its stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and apply the cautery to the joint flat on a piece of cloth equally, and examine every hour of the day or night, that the broken limb does not move, or the ligaments are not softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	If the patient is encouraged by the power of medicine, and the meat that we have placed before, in a manner that the meat is at the first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to eat again, it should be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be eaten in forty days after all;
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then it must be peeled and administer the balms and medicines of ointments for the limb to increase.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is crooked and swollen, it may take 1 or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", from which one is small and is the one that teaches the pouch;
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the others are great, and is the one that is dislocated, near the small bone;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	by chance the large bone alone breaks, or the small ones, and by chance together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the large bone is broken, then the healing is bad, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it is necessary to extend them slightly and align them evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large bone, then it must be strained more strongly;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it over the wrist, and tie the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small ones lower than the others, and let the pains cross over itself, and the wrist in front of it higher, so that the pains suffer no labor.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the ministers' arms to the part below the shoulder, or to the elbow, and other ministers to the upper part.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no piece that can be held, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the broken bone, I have spoken of it in the chapter on singularity;
si pren la cure.	if take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if at the beginning of restoration, abscesses occur, then apply a poultice made of red oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and bind the poultice gently, until the abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the crust, and put the plaster of powder from the mill with abundance of honey, then place the splints, and let the splint of the broken part be slightly outwards, and a bit wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and let it have six splints or arms in many positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	so that the broken part is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and held higher than the broken part, and always less far away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are on the broken part be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough;
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the son, from whom it is strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must raise the limb with hot water, until those itches are soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be too tightly rested.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the strapping, and if the joint is dislocated and the bones are broken, or similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the swelling has passed, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to harm, then let it wait for 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or inquire within, then let the hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and guard against movement and degumming, and sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and let it be known that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	After the back of the hand and to us there are few breaks, and it only happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the bone of the hand is broken or splintered, it is necessary that the hairs lie crossed and straight in front of him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then place his hand on the extended table, and extend the bones broken by the ministrants, and put them evenly in their places until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And apply the plaster and bandages, if there are abscesses not present, then place a splint according to the amount of the limb.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the broken bone is on the outer side of the back of the palm, then make a roll of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken hand.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then strain a long rope, and place it under the knee as wide as the sole of the foot, and strain it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the bone is broken in the posterior region, it is necessary to place a splint above and another below in the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and stabilize the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the broken bone comes to one of the ends, if it is the shoulder, then put it even, as it should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And strain with the sole, and if you see that put a straight small rod to lift the broken bone, and do not move it.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the broken bone is at other ends, such as in the index or the other, then put it even, and tie it with the healthy joint that is next.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	where you tie them all together, as much as is necessary, or place them on a stick, like a bundle.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and disposition of abscesses, and secure what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The teeth of the jaw are often broken, and well seen when it turns in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is as one ties them together above the fracture, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the hairs are cut across his face, then each assistant ties their cord to their equal part.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and it is when the fracture is inserted into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the rib, then one of the ribs towards the base, and the other ribs outside the broken part.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is close to the groin, and then the tendons over the groin are stretched, and the extension downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Then place the bone in its natural position with both hands, as long as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and tie it, if there are no abscesses.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess, let it subside first, then return to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap the injured and swollen part in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then bend the leg until the toes reach the base of the heel, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg, outside the groin, and bring the end of the thread upwards.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	then turn back up the leg and up the thigh the bend, then put on the broken bones, and put a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	then apply the limb's own cloth between the leg and thigh to equalize the strain, then begin to bandage about three or four times over the broken bones.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher than the broken bones, and lessen the strain.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then insert two of the strings that you have rolled between the leg and thigh, and bandage three splints that are above, then return to the outside at the top of the string, as far as you come over the bone.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and the restriction, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, then no abscess or swelling or similar thing comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there is, dislocate it, and direct what comes, as we have said many times;
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if it has pieces of bone that prick, it must be removed if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if not, then it is necessary to cut the limb and draw out the splinters.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the ribs thus that one puts these, as in the shoulder or arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Therefore, in this restoration made thus, it does not hurt the limbs.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is important that the ribs are restored at different times, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the road of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that on the road of the gentleman there is little breakage, but it rains many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a puncture, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and this feels very bad.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is such that one puts together what is broken to its two, as much as it can be assembled together.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and if you have the skill, put on a round bandage, and stretch it as it should be, then warm up all the positions that we have said in other breakages, such as abscess and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply to each accident what it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Note that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "tibia" on the right, and the other is called "fibula".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and can break anything as it comes to the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is like that of the broken arm equally, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg from all parts returns.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it can be seen well.
et torne desoz.	and returns dislocated.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Then relieve the extension, and make it even, and tie the tendons equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but anyway, it is necessary that the fracture is straight, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is less and lighter;
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And the physician according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that gird the leg on one side and the other, and be long enough to go from the knee down to the ankle.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap them around the leg above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, so that the leg will not incline to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one administers the long cloth of the leg, and it is of cloth, and put the leg for support to prevent movement, and properly done, they put it in the break or where he was wounded.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and move each leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the healer is healthy until then.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the breaking of bones due to piers
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breaking of bones, but in the case of piers, there is never breaking of bones and it is not necessary, and only a slight injury occurs in some cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has bones that are slightly broken, and you see these bones overlapping each other, if you put them on the ground like they want to walk, then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are lifted, then press them so much until they return to their place;
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	then put the plaster and poultice on top, and put some cotton on the belly of the foot, then wrap it around the leg evenly, then wrap other cloths around, and other things that you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is released, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if there are any of the two broken, restore them as we have said for the two bones of the hand.
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	Then place a splint along the length of the broken bone, and make it slightly wider, then put the painful part of the splint that I mentioned, and tighten gradually.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	And if there are two or three or more broken bones, place a splint along each length, wrapped in a piece of linen, and tighten the painful part outside the splint.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And make sure it is above the head of the splint under the belly of the bone, so that it presses well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, since we have already mentioned them.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each event as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the jaw of the woman is fractured, if the tooth is loosened, then incline it to the back part, and hold it from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the cavity of the jaw with cotton, and put in as much as is needed.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then lift the woman, and slowly raise her back, and then jump the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the jaw, and then return the bone with the cotton.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has done so, return it, and thus do this seven times a day:
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if she will be healed of the fracture, and if you see, take a bandage of burdock, and tie it around the wound, and blow all the bandage in its natural state;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the bandage in a way that the bandage is inflated inside:
